2:22:1224:0:14:72:345:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Macroeconomics With Heterogeneity: A Practical Guide
2:23:1276:14:14:72:143:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Fatih Guvenen
2:24:1289:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 17622
2:25:1317:14:14:72:262:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:November 2011, Revised January 2012
2:26:1352:14:28:72:234:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:JEL No. E1,E13,E21,E24,E32,E6
2:27:1381:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:28:1389:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:This article reviews macroeconomic models with heterogeneous households. A key question for the
2:29:1484:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:relevance of these models concerns the degree to which markets are complete. This is because the
2:30:1580:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:existence of complete markets imposes restrictions on (i) how much heterogeneity matters for aggregate
2:31:1682:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:phenomena and (ii) the types of cross-sectional distributions that can be obtained. The degree of market
2:32:1786:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:incompleteness, in turn, depends on two factors: (i) the richness of insurance opportunities provided
2:33:1887:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:by the economic environment and (ii) the nature and magnitude of idiosyncratic risks to be insured.
2:34:1986:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:First, I review a broad collection of empirical evidence—from econometric tests of “full insurance,”
2:35:2086:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:to quantitative and empirical analyses of the permanent income (“self-insurance”) model that examine
2:36:2186:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:how it fits the facts about life cycle allocations, to studies that try to directly measure where economies
2:37:2293:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:place between these two benchmarks (“partial insurance”). The empirical evidence I survey reveals
2:38:2390:14:14:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:significant uncertainty in the profession regarding the magnitudes of idiosyncratic risks as well as
2:39:2490:14:14:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:whether or not these risks have increased since the 1970s. An important difficulty stems from the fact
2:40:2592:14:14:72:540:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:that inequality often arises from a mixture of idiosyncratic risk and fixed (or predictable) heterogeneity,
2:41:2699:14:14:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:making the two challenging to disentangle. I also discuss applications of incomplete markets models
2:42:2798:14:14:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:to trends in wealth, consumption, and earnings inequality both over the life cycle and over time, where
2:43:2901:14:14:72:540:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:this challenge is evident. Third, I discuss “approximate” aggregation—the finding that some incomplete
2:44:3003:14:14:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:markets models generate aggregate implications very similar to representative-agent models. What
2:45:3099:14:14:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:approximate aggregation does and does not imply is illustrated through several examples. Finally,
2:46:3196:14:14:72:540:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:I discuss some computational issues relevant for solving and calibrating such models and I provide
2:47:3294:14:14:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:a simple yet fully parallelizable global optimization algorithm that can be used to calibrate heterogeneous
2:48:3401:14:42:72:139:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:agent models.
2:49:3414:42:14:72:143:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Fatih Guvenen
2:50:3427:14:14:72:198:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Department of Economics
2:51:3450:14:14:72:189:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:University of Minnesota
2:52:3473:14:14:72:163:224:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:4-151 Hanson Hall
2:53:3490:14:14:72:193:210:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:1925 Fourth Street South
2:54:3514:14:14:72:193:196:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Minneapolis, MN, 55455
2:55:3536:14:14:72:124:182:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:56:3544:14:0:72:165:168:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:guvenen@umn.edu
3:57:3559:0:20:101:506:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:What is the origin of inequality among men and is it authorized by natural law?
3:58:3638:20:46:210:505:676:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:—Academy of Dijon, 1754 (Theme for essay competition)
3:59:3691:46:32:72:220:630:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:1Introduction
3:60:3704:32:16:72:535:598:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The quest for the origins of inequality has kept philosophers and scientists occupied for
3:61:3793:16:16:72:535:582:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:centuries. A central question of interest—also highlighted in Academy of Dijon’s solicitation
3:62:3886:16:16:72:535:566:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for its essay competition1—is whether inequality is determined solely through a natural
3:63:3973:16:16:71:535:550:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:process or through the interaction of innate differences with man-made institutions and
3:64:4060:16:15:71:534:534:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:policies. And, if it is the latter, what is the precise relationship between these origins and
3:65:4154:15:21:71:194:519:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:socio-economic policies?
3:66:4178:21:16:89:535:498:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:While many interesting ideas and hypotheses have been put forward over time, the main
3:67:4263:16:15:71:535:482:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:impediment to progress came from the difficulty of scientifically testing these hypotheses,
3:68:4354:15:16:71:534:467:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which would allow researchers to refine ideas that were deemed promising and discard those
3:69:4444:16:16:71:534:451:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that were not. Economists, who grapple with the same questions today, have three impor-
3:70:4531:16:16:71:534:435:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tant advantages that can allow us to make progress. First, modern quantitative economics
3:71:4619:16:16:71:534:419:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:provides a wide set of powerful tools, which allow researchers to build “laboratories” in which
3:72:4714:16:16:71:533:403:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:various hypotheses regarding the origins and consequences of inequality can be studied. Sec-
3:73:4806:16:16:71:534:387:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ond, the widespread availability of rich micro data sources—from cross-sectional surveys to
3:74:4897:16:16:71:534:371:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:panel datasets from administrative records that contain millions of observations—provides
3:75:4986:16:16:71:534:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fresh input into these laboratories. Third, thanks to Moore’s law, the cost of computation
3:76:5076:16:15:71:534:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:has fallen radically in the past decades, making it feasible to numerically solve, simulate, and
3:77:5172:15:16:71:534:324:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:estimate complex models with rich heterogeneity on a typical desktop workstation available
3:78:5262:16:21:71:173:308:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to most economists.
3:79:5281:21:15:89:535:287:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:There are two broad sets of economic questions for which economists might want to
3:80:5362:15:16:71:534:272:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model heterogeneity.  First, and most obviously, these models allow us to study cross-
3:81:5448:16:16:71:534:256:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sectional, or distributional, phenomena. The US economy today provides ample motivation
3:82:5535:16:16:71:534:240:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for studying distributional issues, with the top 1% of households owning almost half of
3:83:5622:16:16:71:534:224:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:all stocks and 1/3 of all net worth in the United States, and wage inequality having risen
3:84:5712:16:16:71:534:208:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:virtually without interruption for the lastfortyyears. Not surprisingly, many questions of
3:85:5802:16:16:71:534:192:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:current policy debate are inherently about their distributional consequences. For example,
3:86:5892:16:16:71:534:176:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heated disagreements about major budget issues—such as reforming Medicare, Medicaid,
3:87:5976:16:16:71:534:160:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and the Social Security system—often revolve around the redistributional effects of such
3:88:6064:16:15:71:534:144:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:changes. Similarly, a crucial aspect of the current debate on taxation is about “who should
3:89:6155:15:16:71:534:129:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:pay what?”.  Answering these questions would begin with a sound understanding of the
3:90:6239:16:18:71:367:113:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fundamental determinants of different types of inequality.
3:91:6297:18:15:85:534:95:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:1The competition generated broad interest from scholars of the time, including Jean-Jacques Rousseau,
3:92:6398:15:0:71:529:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:who wrote his famousDiscourse on the Origins of Inequalityin response, but failed to win the top prize.
4:93:6502:0:16:89:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:A second set of questions for which heterogeneity could matter involve aggregate phe-
4:94:6587:16:16:71:534:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nomena.  This second use of heterogeneous-agent models is less obvious than the first,
4:95:6673:16:16:71:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:because various aggregation theorems as well as numerical results (e.g.,Rios-Rull(1996)
4:96:6760:16:16:71:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and   Krusell and Smith(1998)) have established that certain types of heterogeneity do not
4:97:6850:16:21:71:427:632:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:change (many) implications relative to a representative-agent model.2
4:98:6919:21:16:89:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To understand this result and its ramifications, in Section 2, I start by reviewing some
4:99:7007:16:16:71:535:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:key theoretical results on aggregation (Rubinstein(1974)andConstantinides(1982)). Our
4:100:7092:16:16:71:534:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:interest in these theorems comes from a practical concern: basically, a subset of the condi-
4:101:7184:16:15:71:534:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tions required by these theorems are often satisfied in heterogeneous-agent models, making
4:102:7274:15:16:71:534:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:their aggregate implications closely mimic those from a representative-agent economy. For
4:103:7363:16:16:71:538:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:example, an important theorem proved byConstantinides(1982)establishestheexistence
4:104:7445:16:16:71:534:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of a representative agent if markets are complete.3This central role of complete markets
4:105:7533:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:turned the spotlight since the late 1980s onto its testable implications for perfect risk sharing
4:106:7630:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(or “full insurance”). As I review in Section 3, these implications have been tested by an ex-
4:107:7724:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tensive literature using datasets from all around the world—from developed countries such
4:108:7813:16:16:72:535:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as the United States to village economies in India, Thailand, Uganda, and so on. While
4:109:7899:16:16:72:535:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this literature delivered a clearstatisticalrejection, it also revealed a surprising amount
4:110:7990:16:15:72:535:420:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of “partial” insurance, in the sense that individual consumption growth (or, more gener-
4:111:8078:15:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ally, marginal utility growth) does not seem to respond to many seemingly large shocks,
4:112:8165:16:16:72:539:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:such as long spells of unemployment, strikes, and involuntary moves (Cochrane(1991)and
4:113:8251:16:21:72:242:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Townsend(1994), among others).
4:114:8281:21:16:89:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This raises the more practical question of “howfarare we from the complete markets
4:115:8363:16:16:72:536:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:benchmark?”. To answer this question, researchers have recently turned to directly measur-
4:116:8453:16:16:72:535:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ing the degree of partial insurance, defined for our purposes as the degree of consumption
4:117:8543:16:16:72:534:304:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:smoothing over and above what an individual can achieve on her own via “self-insurance”
4:118:8630:16:15:72:535:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in a permanent income model (i.e., using a single risk-free asset for borrowing and saving).
4:119:8722:15:16:72:535:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Although this literature is quite new—and so a definitive answer is still not on hand—it is
4:120:8813:16:21:72:394:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:likely to remain an active area of research in the coming years.
4:121:8877:21:16:89:535:236:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The empirical rejection of the complete markets hypothesis launched an enormous liter-
4:122:8963:16:16:72:535:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ature on incomplete markets models starting in the early 1990s, which I discuss in Section
4:123:9053:16:16:72:535:204:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:4. Starting withImrohoroglu(1989),Huggett(1993), andAiyagari(1994), this literature
4:124:9136:16:16:72:535:188:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:has been addressing issues from a very broad spectrum, covering diverse topics such as the
4:125:9226:16:16:72:535:172:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equity premium and other puzzles in finance; important life cycle choices, such as education,
4:126:9319:16:16:72:535:156:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:marriage/divorce, housing purchases, fertility choice, etc.; aggregate and distributional ef-
4:127:9412:16:17:72:535:140:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fects of a variety of policies ranging from capital and labor income taxation to the overhaul
4:128:9505:17:16:85:535:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:2These aggregation results donotimply that all aspects of a representative-agent model will be the same
4:129:9608:16:8:72:534:107:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:as those of the underlying individual problem. I discuss important examples to the contrary in Section7.2.
4:130:9714:8:16:85:534:99:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:3(Financial) markets are “complete” when agents have access to a sufficiently rich set of assets that allows
4:131:9822:16:0:71:456:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:them to transfer their wealth/resources across any two dates and/or states of the world.
5:132:9911:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of Social Security, reforming the health care system, among many others. An especially im-
5:133:10001:16:16:72:536:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:portant set of applications concerns trends in wealth, consumption, and earnings inequality.
5:134:10093:16:20:72:240:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:These are discussed in Section 5.
5:135:10126:20:16:89:537:644:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Acriticalpre-requisitefortheseanalysesisthedisentanglingof“exanteheterogeneity”
5:136:10205:16:16:72:535:628:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from “risk/uncertainty” (also called ex post heterogeneity)—two sides of the same coin,
5:137:10292:16:16:72:534:612:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with potentially very different implications for policy and welfare. But this is a challenging
5:138:10386:16:16:72:535:596:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:task, because inequality often arises from a mixture of heterogeneity and idiosyncratic
5:139:10473:16:15:72:535:580:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:risk, making the two difficult to disentangle. It requires researchers to carefully combine
5:140:10564:15:16:72:534:565:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cross-sectional information with sufficiently long time-series data for analysis. The state-
5:141:10656:16:16:72:535:549:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of-the-art methods used in this field increasingly blend the set of tools developed and used
5:142:10748:16:16:72:535:533:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by quantitative macroeconomists with those used by structural econometricians. Despite
5:143:10834:16:16:72:535:517:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the application of these sophisticated tools, there remains significant uncertainty in the
5:144:10924:16:16:72:535:501:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:profession regarding the magnitudes of idiosyncratic risks as well as whether or not these
5:145:11014:16:20:72:257:485:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:risks have increased since the 1970s.
5:146:11051:20:16:89:535:465:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The Imrohoroglu-Huggett-Aiyagari framework sidestepped a difficult issue raised by the
5:147:11137:16:16:72:535:449:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lack of aggregation—that aggregates, including prices, depend on the entire wealth distribu-
5:148:11229:16:15:72:535:433:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tion. This was accomplished by abstracting from aggregate shocks, which allowed them to
5:149:11316:15:16:72:535:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:focus on stationary equilibria in which prices (the interest rate and the average wage) were
5:150:11408:16:16:72:535:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:simply some constants to be solved for in equilibrium. A far more challenging problem with
5:151:11498:16:16:72:535:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:incomplete markets arises in the presence of aggregate shocks, in which case equilibrium
5:152:11586:16:16:72:535:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:prices becomefunctionsof the entire wealth distribution, which varies with the aggregate
5:153:11674:16:16:72:535:354:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:state. Individuals need to know these equilibrium functions, so that they can forecast how
5:154:11764:16:16:72:535:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:prices will evolve in the future as the aggregate state evolves in a stochastic manner. Be-
5:155:11855:16:16:72:535:322:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cause the wealth distribution is an infinite-dimensional object, an exact solution is typically
5:156:11950:16:16:72:535:306:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:not feasible.Krusell and Smith(1998) proposed a solution whereby one approximates the
5:157:12035:16:15:72:535:290:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wealth distribution with a finite number of its moments (inspired by the idea that a given
5:158:12125:15:16:72:535:275:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:probability distribution can be represented by its moment generating function). In a re-
5:159:12213:16:16:72:535:259:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:markable finding, they showed that the first moment (the mean) of the wealth distribution
5:160:12302:16:16:72:535:243:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:was all individuals needed to track in this economy for predicting all future prices. This
5:161:12392:16:16:72:535:227:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:result—generally known as “approximate aggregation”—is a double-edged sword. On the
5:162:12475:16:16:72:535:211:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:one hand, it makes feasible the solution of a wide range of interesting models with incomplete
5:163:12569:16:16:72:535:195:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:markets and aggregate shocks. On the other hand, it suggests that ex post heterogeneity
5:164:12656:16:16:72:535:179:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:does not often generate aggregate implications much different from a representative-agent
5:165:12745:16:16:72:535:163:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model. So, the hope that some aggregate phenomena that were puzzling in representative-
5:166:12832:16:15:72:535:147:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:agent models could be explained in an incomplete markets framework is weakened with this
5:167:12920:15:16:72:535:132:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:result. While this is an important finding, there are many examples where heterogeneity
5:168:13007:16:20:72:479:116:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f2:doesaffect aggregates in a significant way. I discuss a variety of such examples.
5:169:13088:20:16:89:535:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Finally, I turn to computation and calibration. First, in Section 6, I discuss some details
5:170:13179:16:0:72:535:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the Krusell-Smith method. A number of potential pitfalls are discussed and alternative
6:171:13269:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:checks of accuracy are studied. Second, an important practical issue that arises with cali-
6:172:13360:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:brating/estimating large and complex quantitative models is the following. The objective
6:173:13448:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:function that we minimize often has lots of jaggedness, small jumps, and/or deep ridges
6:174:13535:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:due to a variety of reasons that have to do with approximations, interpolations, binding
6:175:13623:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:constraints, etc. Thus, local optimization methods are typically of little help on their own,
6:176:13716:16:16:72:536:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:because they very often get stuck in some local minima. In Section 8, I describe a global
6:177:13805:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:optimization algorithm that is simple yet powerful and is fully parallelizable without re-
6:178:13895:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:quiring any knowledge of MPI, OpenMP, and so on. It works on any number of computers
6:179:13979:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that are connected to the Internet and have access to a synchronization service like Drop-
6:180:14069:15:16:72:534:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Box. I provide a discussion of ways to customize this algorithm with different options to
6:181:14158:16:40:72:132:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:experiment.
6:182:14169:40:33:72:218:497:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:2Aggregation
6:183:14181:33:15:72:535:464:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Even in a simple static model with no uncertainty we need a way to deal with consumer
6:184:14266:15:16:72:535:449:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneity. Adding dynamics and risk into this environment make things more complex
6:185:14352:16:16:72:535:433:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and require a different set of conditions to be imposed. In this section, I will review some key
6:186:14448:16:16:72:535:417:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:theoretical results on various forms of aggregation. I begin with a very simple framework
6:187:14537:16:16:72:535:401:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and build up to a fully dynamic model with idiosyncratic (i.e., individual-specific) risk and
6:188:14630:16:21:72:530:385:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discuss what types of aggregation results one can hope to get and under what conditions.
6:189:14718:21:16:89:535:364:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Our interest in aggregation is not mainly for theoretical reasons.  As we shall see,
6:190:14802:16:16:72:535:348:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:some of the conditions required for aggregation are satisfied (sometimes inadvertently!)
6:191:14890:16:15:72:535:332:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by commonly used heterogeneous-agent frameworks, making them behave very much like
6:192:14972:15:16:72:541:317:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:arepresentative-agentmodel. Althoughthisoftenmakesthemodeleasiertosolvenu-
6:193:15046:16:16:72:535:301:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:merically, at the same time it can make its implications “boring”—i.e., too similar to a
6:194:15134:16:16:72:535:285:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:representative-agent model. Thus, learning about the assumptions underlying the aggrega-
6:195:15222:16:16:72:535:269:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tion theorems can allow model builders to choose the features of their models carefully so
6:196:15312:16:34:72:209:253:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as to avoid such outcomes.

9:303:20008:16:16:71:534:617:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f6:of return are determined in cases (2) to (6) as if there exists only composite individuals
9:304:20098:16:0:71:427:601:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f14:each with the following economic characteristics: (i) Resources:w0=
9:305:20165:0:9:430:443:610:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:P
9:306:20166:9:16:445:539:601:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f6:wi0/I;(ii)Tastes:
9:307:20183:16:0:72:142:585:143:g_d0_f19:64:g_d0_f15:-=⇧(-i)(⇢i/
9:308:20194:0:8:144:158:596:64:g_d0_f32:64:g_d0_f27:P⇢
9:309:20196:8:19:158:541:588:36:g_d0_f26:143:g_d0_f6:i)(where-⌘1/--1)or-=P-i/I;and(iv)preferenceparameters
9:310:20249:19:0:71:90:569:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f14:⇢=
9:311:20251:0:9:93:106:578:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:P
9:312:20252:9:33:108:170:569:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f6:⇢i/I,and-.
9:313:20262:33:31:89:237:536:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Several remarks are in order.
9:314:20291:31:16:72:535:505:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Demand Aggregation.An important corollary to this theorem is that whenever a com-
9:315:20372:16:16:72:536:489:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:posite consumer can be constructed, in equilibrium, rates of return are insensitive to the
9:316:20462:16:15:72:535:473:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:distribution of resources among individuals. This is because the aggregate demand functions
9:317:20553:15:16:72:535:458:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(for both consumption and assets) depend only on total wealth and not on its distribution.
9:318:20643:16:31:72:264:442:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Thus, we have “demand aggregation.”
9:319:20678:31:16:72:534:411:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Aggregation and Heterogeneity in Relative Risk Aversion.Notice that all six cases
9:320:20759:16:16:72:535:395:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that give rise to demand aggregation in the theorem require individuals to have the same
9:321:20847:16:15:72:535:379:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:curvature parameter,-. To see why this is important, note that (with HARA preferences)
9:322:20933:15:16:71:535:364:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f14:the optimal holdings of the risky asset is a linear function of the consumer’s wealth:1+
9:323:21022:16:16:72:535:348:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f2:2wt/-,where1and2are some constants that depend on the properties of returns. It
9:324:21104:16:16:71:535:332:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is easy to see that with identical slopes,2/-, it does not matter who holds the wealth.
9:325:21192:16:16:72:535:316:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In other words, redistributing wealth between any two agents would cause changes in total
9:326:21281:16:16:72:535:300:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:demand for assets that will cancel out each other, due to linearity and same slopes. Notice
9:327:21372:16:16:72:535:284:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:also that while identical curvature is a necessary condition, it is not sufficient for demand
9:328:21465:16:16:72:535:268:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregation: each of the six cases adds more conditions on top of this identical curvature
9:329:21555:16:34:72:140:252:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:requirement.8
9:330:21568:34:28:72:437:218:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:2.3  A Dynamic Economy (WithIdiosyncratic Risk)
9:331:21615:28:16:72:535:190:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:WhileRubinstein(1974)’s theorem delivers a strong aggregation result, it achieves this by
9:332:21704:16:16:71:534:174:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:abstracting from a key aspect of dynamic economies: uncertainty that evolves over time.
9:333:21791:16:16:71:534:158:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Almost every interesting economy that we discuss in the coming sections will feature some
9:334:21880:16:19:71:534:142:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:kind of idiosyncratic risk that individuals face (coming from labor income fluctuations,
9:335:21968:19:15:85:535:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:8Notice also that, because in some cases (such as (2)) heterogeneity in⇢is allowed, individuals will
9:336:22068:15:12:72:534:108:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:exhibit different relative risk aversions (if they have differentwt), for example in the generalized CRRA
9:337:22173:12:0:71:213:96:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:case, and still allow aggregation.
10:338:22208:0:16:72:534:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:shocks to health, shocks to housing prices and asset returns, among others).Rubinstein
10:339:22294:16:20:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1974)’s theorem is silent about how the aggregate economy behaves under these scenarios.
10:340:22383:20:16:89:534:660:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This is whereConstantinides(1982) comes into play: He shows that if markets are
10:341:22462:16:16:72:535:644:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:complete, under much weaker conditions (on preferences, beliefs, discount rates, etc.) one
10:342:22552:16:16:72:535:628:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can replace heterogeneous consumers with a planner who maximizes a weighted sum of
10:343:22634:16:16:72:535:612:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumers’ utilities. In turn, the central planner can be replaced by a composite consumer
10:344:22724:16:19:72:379:596:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:who maximizes a utility function of aggregate consumption.
10:345:22782:19:16:89:535:577:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To show this, consider a private ownership economy with production as inDebreu(1959),
10:346:22867:16:16:72:535:561:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:withmconsumers,nfirms, andlcommodities. As inDebreu(1959), these commodities
10:347:22943:16:16:72:539:545:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can be thought of a date-event labelled goods (and concave utility functions,Ui,asbeing
10:348:23030:16:16:72:535:529:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:defined over these goods) allowing us to map these results into an intertemporal economy
10:349:23118:16:16:72:534:513:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with uncertainty. Consumeriis endowed with wealth(wi1,wi2,...,wil)and shares of firms
10:350:23203:16:0:71:233:497:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f2:(✓i1,✓i2,...,✓in)with✓ij-0and
10:351:23232:0:12:236:249:506:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:P
10:352:23233:12:13:248:535:494:64:g_d0_f15:143:g_d0_f2:m✓ij=1.LetthevectorsCiandYjdenote, respectively,
10:353:23281:13:20:71:371:481:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuali’s consumption set and firmj’s production set.
10:354:23338:20:16:89:535:461:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:An equilibrium is an(m+n+1)-tuple((c⇤i)mi=1,(y⇤j)nj=1,p⇤)such that, as usual, con-
10:355:23420:16:15:71:534:445:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sumers maximize utility, firms maximize their profits, and markets clear. Under standard
10:356:23508:15:20:71:362:430:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:assumptions an equilibrium exists and is Pareto optimal.

11:390:24054:0:16:89:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Now, given the production sets of each firm and the aggregate endowments of each

11:420:24638:0:42:428:531:452:64:g_d0_f28:143:g_d0_f6:⇤)is an equilibrium.
11:421:24658:42:16:72:535:410:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Constantinides versus Rubinstein.Constantinides allows for much more generality
11:422:24737:16:16:72:535:394:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:than Rubinstein by relaxing two important restrictions. First, no conditions are imposed
11:423:24825:16:16:72:535:378:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on the homogeneity of preferences, which was a crucial element in every version of Rubin-
11:424:24914:16:16:72:535:362:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stein’s theorem. Second, Constantinides allows for both exogenous endowment as well as
11:425:25000:16:16:72:535:346:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:production at every date and state. In contrast, recall that, in Rubinstein’s environment,
11:426:25090:16:16:72:535:330:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuals start life with a wealth stock and receive no further income or endowment dur-
11:427:25180:16:15:72:535:314:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ing life. In exchange, Constantinides requires complete markets and does not get demand
11:428:25267:15:16:72:535:299:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregation. Notice that the existence of a composite consumer does not imply demand
11:429:25351:16:16:72:535:283:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregation, for at least two reasons.  First, composite demand depends on the weights
11:430:25437:16:16:72:535:267:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in the planner’s problem and, thus, depends on the distribution of endowments. Second,
11:431:25523:16:16:72:534:251:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f6:the composite is defined at equilibrium prices and no claim is made that its demandcurve
11:432:25611:16:21:72:296:235:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:coincides with the aggregate demand curve.
11:433:25653:21:16:89:535:214:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Thus, the usefulness of Constantinides’ result hinges on (i) the degree to which markets
11:434:25741:16:16:72:535:198:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:are complete, (ii) whether we want to allow for idiosyncratic risk and heterogeneity in
11:435:25828:16:16:72:535:182:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:preferences (which are both restricted in Rubinstein’s theorem), and (iii) whether or not we
11:436:25920:16:15:72:535:166:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:need demand aggregation. Below I will address these issues in more detail. We will see that,
11:437:26012:15:16:72:535:151:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:interestingly, even when markets are not complete, in certain cases, we will not only get
11:438:26101:16:16:72:535:135:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:close to a composite consumer representation, but we can also get quite close to the much
11:439:26190:16:16:72:535:119:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stronger result of demand aggregation! An important reason for this outcome is that many
11:440:26278:16:16:72:535:103:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneous-agent models assume identical preferences, which eliminates an important
11:441:26364:16:0:72:535:87:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:source of heterogeneity, satisfying Rubinstein’s conditions for preferences. However, these
12:442:26457:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:models do feature idiosyncratic risk, but as we shall we, when the planning horizon is long,
12:443:26549:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:such shocks can often be smoothed effectively using even a simple risk free asset. More on
12:444:26639:16:31:72:212:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this in the coming sections.
12:445:26667:31:15:72:534:633:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Completing Markets by Adding Financial Assets.It is useful to distinguish between
12:446:26748:15:16:72:535:618:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:“physical” assets—those in positive net supply (e.g. equity shares, capital, housing, etc)—
12:447:26839:16:16:72:535:602:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and “financial” assets—those in zero net supply (bonds, insurance contracts, etc.).  The
12:448:26927:16:16:72:535:586:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:latter are simply some contracts written on a piece of paper that specifies the conditions
12:449:27017:16:16:72:535:570:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:under which one agent transfers resources to another one. In principle, it can be created
12:450:27106:16:16:72:535:554:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with little cost. Now suppose that we live in a world withJphysical assets and that there
12:451:27195:16:16:72:535:538:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:areS(>J)states of the world. In this general setting, markets are incomplete. However, if
12:452:27284:16:16:72:535:522:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumers have homogenous tastes, endowments, and beliefs, then markets are (effectively)
12:453:27373:16:16:72:535:506:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:complete by simply adding enoughfinancialassets (in zero net supply). There is no loss of
12:454:27462:16:15:72:535:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:optimality and nothing will change by this action, because in equilibrium identical agents
12:455:27552:15:16:72:535:475:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:will not trade with each other. The bottom line is that the more “homogeneity” we are
12:456:27637:16:16:72:535:459:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:willing to assume among consumers, the less demanding the complete markets assumption
12:457:27722:16:40:72:445:443:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:becomes. This point should be kept in mind as we will return to it later.
12:458:27795:40:33:72:387:403:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:3EmpiricalEvidenceonInsurance
12:459:27824:33:16:72:535:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Dynamic economic models with heterogeneity typically feature individual-specific uncer-
12:460:27911:16:16:72:535:354:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tainty that evolves over time—coming from fluctuations in labor earnings, health status,
12:461:27999:16:16:72:536:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:portfolio returns, among others.  Although this structure does not fit into Rubinstein’s
12:462:28087:16:15:72:535:322:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:environment, it is covered by Constantinides’ theorem, which requires complete markets.
12:463:28174:15:16:72:535:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f6:Thus, a key empirical question isthe extent to which complete markets can serve as a useful
12:464:28265:16:16:72:535:291:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f2:benchmarkand a good approximation to the world we live in. As we shall see in this section,
12:465:28356:16:21:72:411:275:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the answer turns out to be more nuanced than a simple yes or no.
12:466:28420:21:16:89:534:254:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To explain the broad variety of evidence that has been brought to bear on this question,
12:467:28508:16:16:72:539:238:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this section is structured in the following way. First, in Section3.1,Ibeginbydiscussing
12:468:28596:16:16:72:541:222:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:alargeempiricalliteraturethathastestedakeypredictionofcompletemarkets—that
12:469:28670:16:16:72:535:206:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:marginal utility growth is equated across individuals.  This is often called “perfect” or
12:470:28759:16:16:72:544:190:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:“full” insurance, and it is soundly rejected in the data. Section3.2  discusses an alternative
12:471:28853:16:15:72:535:174:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:benchmark, inspired by this rejection.  This is the permanent income model, in which
12:472:28937:15:16:72:535:159:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuals have access to only borrowing and saving—or “self insurance.” In a way, this is
12:473:29028:16:16:72:535:143:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the other extreme end of the insurance spectrum. Finally, Section3.3 discusses studies that
12:474:29119:16:16:72:535:127:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:take an intermediate view—“partial insurance”—and provide some evidence to support it.
12:475:29205:16:0:72:308:111:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:We now begin with the tests of full insurance.
13:476:29253:0:29:72:309:696:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:3.1  Benchmark 1: Full Insurance
13:477:29285:29:16:72:535:667:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To develop the theoretical framework underlying the empirical analyses, start with an econ-
13:478:29376:16:16:72:535:651:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:omy populated by agents who derive utility from consumptionctas well as some other
13:479:29458:16:0:72:149:635:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f15:good(s)dt:Ui
13:480:29470:0:10:151:156:645:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:-
13:481:29471:10:0:157:201:635:143:g_d0_f13:64:g_d0_f17:cit+1,dit+1
13:482:29482:0:10:202:207:645:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:-
13:483:29483:10:16:207:535:635:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:, whereiindexes individuals.  These other goods can include
13:484:29542:16:16:71:534:619:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:leisure time (of husband and wife if the unit of analysis is a household), children, lagged
13:485:29633:16:20:71:400:603:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumption (as in habit formation models), so on and so forth.
13:486:29696:20:16:89:535:583:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The key implication of perfect insurance can be derived by following two distinct ap-
13:487:29781:16:16:71:534:567:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:proaches. The first environment assumes a social planner who pools all individuals’ resources
13:488:29874:16:16:71:534:551:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and maximizes a social welfare function that assigns a positive weight to every individual.
13:489:29965:16:16:71:534:535:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In the second environment, allocations are determined in a competitive equilibrium of a
13:490:30052:16:16:71:534:519:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:frictionless economy where individuals are able to trade in a complete set of financial secu-
13:491:30145:16:16:71:534:503:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rities. Both of these frameworks make the following strong prediction for the growth rate
13:492:30234:16:41:71:238:487:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of individuals’ marginal utilities:
13:493:30269:41:0:240:249:446:143:g_d0_f19:64:g_d0_f15:-i
13:494:30271:0:0:250:262:455:143:g_d0_f13:64:g_d0_f15:Uic
13:495:30274:0:10:265:270:465:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:-
13:496:30275:10:0:270:315:455:143:g_d0_f13:64:g_d0_f17:cit+1,dit+1
13:497:30286:0:27:316:321:465:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:-
13:498:30287:27:0:262:310:438:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:Uic(cit,dit)
13:499:30299:0:0:326:335:446:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f14:=
13:500:30300:0:16:339:361:454:143:g_d0_f31:64:g_d0_f17:⇤t+1
13:501:30304:16:0:345:356:438:143:g_d0_f31:64:g_d0_f15:⇤t
13:502:30306:0:28:363:535:446:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:,(1)
13:503:30310:28:16:72:535:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:whereUcdenotes the marginal utility of consumption and⇤tis the aggregate shock.9This
13:504:30394:16:16:72:535:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:condition thus says that every individual’s marginal utility must grow in locksteps with the
13:505:30486:16:16:72:535:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate and, hence, with each other. No individual-specific term appears on the right
13:506:30573:16:16:72:535:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:hand side, such as idiosyncratic income shocks, unemployment, sickness, and so on. All
13:507:30659:16:16:72:535:354:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:these idiosyncratic events are perfectly insured in this world. From here one can introduce
13:508:30750:16:27:72:391:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:anumberofadditionalassumptionsforempiricaltractability.
13:509:30805:27:16:72:535:311:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Complete Markets and Cross-Sectional Heterogeneity: A Digression.So far we
13:510:30879:16:15:72:535:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have focused on what market completeness implies for the study of aggregate phenomena
13:511:30964:15:16:72:535:280:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in light of Constantinides’ theorem. However, complete markets also imposes restrictions
13:512:31052:16:16:72:535:264:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on the evolution of thecross-sectional distribution, which can be seen in condition (1).
13:513:31140:16:16:72:539:248:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:For a given specification ofU,condition(1)translatesintorestrictionsontheevolutions
13:514:31223:16:16:72:535:232:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ofctanddt(possibly a vector).  Although, it is possible to chooseUto be sufficiently
13:515:31307:16:16:72:535:216:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:general and flexible (e.g., include preference shifters, assume non-separability) to generate
13:516:31400:16:16:72:535:200:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rich dynamics in cross-sectional distributions, this strategy would attribute all the action
13:517:31492:16:16:72:535:184:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to preferences, which are essentially unobservable. Even in that case, models that are not
13:518:31582:16:16:72:535:168:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bound by (1)—and therefore have idiosyncratic shocks affect individual allocations—can
13:519:31668:16:15:72:535:152:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:generate a much richer set of cross-sectional distributions. Whether that extra richness is
13:520:31759:15:16:72:535:137:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:necessary for explaining salient features of the data is another matter and is not always
13:521:31848:16:19:72:535:121:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:obvious (see, e.g.,Caselli and Ventura(2000),Badel and Huggett(2007), andGuvenen and
13:522:31932:19:15:85:535:102:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:9Alternatively stated,⇤tis the Lagrange multiplier on the aggregate resource constraint at timetin the
13:523:32034:15:0:72:464:87:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:planner’s problem or the state price density in the competitive equilibrium interpretation.
14:524:32127:0:21:72:167:696:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:Kuruscu(2009)).10
14:525:32144:21:21:89:383:675:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Now I return back to the empirical tests of condition (1).
14:526:32202:21:16:89:539:654:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In a pioneering paper,Altug and Miller(1990)werethefirsttoformallytesttheim-
14:527:32278:16:16:71:534:638:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:plications of (1). They considered households as their unit of analysis and specified a rich
14:528:32370:16:16:71:534:622:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Beckerian utility function that included husband’s and wife’s leisure times as well as con-
14:529:32461:16:16:71:534:606:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sumption (food expenditures), and adjusted for demographics (children, age, etc.). Using
14:530:32549:16:16:71:534:590:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:data from the Panel Study of Income Dynamics (PSID) they could not reject full insur-
14:531:32634:16:15:71:539:574:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ance.Hayashi et al.(1996)revisitedthistopicafewyearslaterandusingthesamedata
14:532:32710:15:16:71:535:559:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:set, they rejected perfect risk sharing.11Given this rejection in the whole population, they
14:533:32802:16:16:72:535:543:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:investigated if there might be better insurancewithinfamilies, who presumably have closer
14:534:32891:16:16:72:535:527:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ties with each other than the population at large and could therefore provide insurance to
14:535:32981:16:21:72:513:511:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:the members in need. They found that this hypothesis too was statistically rejected.12
14:536:33067:21:16:89:540:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In a similar vein,Guvenen(2007a)investigatedhowtheextentofrisksharingvaries
14:537:33142:16:16:71:535:474:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:across different wealth groups, such as stockholders and non-stockholders. This question is
14:538:33233:16:16:71:534:458:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:motivated by the observation that stockholders (who made up less than 20% of the pop-
14:539:33318:16:16:71:534:442:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ulation for much of the 20th century) own about 80% of net worth and 90% of financial
14:540:33403:16:15:71:534:426:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wealth in the US economy, and therefore play a disproportionately large role in the deter-
14:541:33493:15:16:71:534:411:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mination of macroeconomic aggregates. On the one hand, these wealthy individuals have
14:542:33578:16:16:71:534:395:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:access to a wide range of financial securities that can presumably allow better risk insurance;
14:543:33673:16:16:71:535:379:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on the other hand, they are exposed to different risks not faced by the less-wealthy non-
14:544:33762:16:16:71:534:363:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stockholders. Using data from the PSID, he strongly rejected perfect risk-sharing among
14:545:33849:16:16:71:534:347:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stockholders, but perhaps surprisingly, did not find evidence against it among nonstockhold-
14:546:33941:16:16:71:535:331:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ers. This finding suggests further focus on risk factors that primarily affect the wealthy, such
14:547:34037:16:21:71:524:315:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as entrepreneurial income risk that is concentrated at the top of the wealth distribution.
14:548:34127:21:16:89:539:294:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Anumberofotherpapersimposedfurtherassumptionsbeforetestingforrisksharing.
14:549:34200:16:15:71:540:278:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Averycommonassumptionistheseparabilitybetweenctanddt,(forexample,leisure),
14:550:34274:15:16:71:534:263:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which leads to an equation that only involves consumption (Cochrane(1991),Attanasio
14:551:34357:16:19:71:535:247:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and Davis(1996),Nelson(1994)).13Assuming power utility in addition to separability, we
14:552:34443:19:15:81:535:228:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:10Caselli and Ventura(2000) show that a wide range of distributional dynamics and income mobility
14:553:34540:15:12:72:535:213:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:patterns can arise in the Cass-Koopmans optimal savings model and in the Arrow-Romer model of pro-
14:554:34638:12:12:72:538:201:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:ductivity spillovers.Badel and Huggett(2007)showthatlifecycleinequalitypatterns(discussedinSection
14:555:34736:12:12:72:539:189:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:3.2)thathavebeenviewedasevidenceofincompletemarketscaninfactbegeneratedusingacomplete
14:556:34821:12:12:72:534:177:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:markets model.Guvenen and Kuruscu(2009) show that a human capital model with heterogeneity in
14:557:34914:12:12:72:535:165:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:learning ability and skill-biased technical change generates rich non-monotonic dynamics consistent with
14:558:35018:12:9:72:526:153:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:the US data since the 1970s, despite featuring no idiosyncratic shocks (and thus has complete markets).
14:559:35121:9:15:81:534:144:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:11Datasets such as the PSID are known to go through regular revisions, which might be able to account
14:560:35222:15:8:71:298:129:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:for the discrepancy between the two papers’ results.
14:561:35274:8:16:81:534:121:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:12This finding has implications for the modeling of the household decision-making process as a unitary
14:562:35376:16:8:71:380:105:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:model as opposed to one in which there is bargaining between spouses.
14:563:35445:8:16:81:535:97:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:13Non-separability, for example between consumption and leisure, can be allowed forifthe planner is
14:564:35544:16:0:71:534:81:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:assumed to be able to transfer leisure freely across individuals. While transfers of consumption are easier to
15:565:35656:0:29:72:490:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can take the logs of both sides of equation (1) and then time-difference to obtain:
15:566:35739:29:29:269:535:667:143:g_d0_f31:143:g_d0_f2:-Ci,t=-⇤t,(2)
15:567:35752:29:16:72:543:638:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:whereCt⌘log(ct)and-Ct⌘Ct-Ct-1.Severalpapershavetestedthispredictionby
15:568:35821:16:29:72:240:622:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:running a regression of the form:
15:569:35854:29:29:235:535:593:143:g_d0_f31:143:g_d0_f2:-Ci,t=-⇤t+ 0Zit+✏i,t,(3)
15:570:35877:29:16:72:535:564:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:where the vectorZitcontains factors that are idiosyncratic to individual/household/group
15:571:35965:16:21:71:497:548:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:i.Perfectinsuranceimpliesthatalltheelementsofthevector are equal to zero.
15:572:36037:21:16:89:538:527:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Cochrane(1991),Mace(1991), andNelson(1994)aretheearlystudiesthatexploitthis
15:573:36112:16:16:72:535:511:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:simple regression structure.Mace(1991) focused on whether or not consumption responded
15:574:36198:16:16:72:535:495:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to idiosyncratic wage shocks: i.e.,Zit=-Wit.14While Mace failed to reject full insurance,
15:575:36287:16:16:72:535:479:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Nelson(1994) later pointed out several issues with the treatment of data (and measurement
15:576:36376:16:16:72:535:463:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:error in particular) that affects Mace’s results. Nelson showed that a more careful treatment
15:577:36469:16:21:72:282:447:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of these issues results in strong rejection.
15:578:36513:21:15:89:535:426:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Cochrane(1991) raised a different point. He argued that studies, such as Mace’s, that
15:579:36598:15:16:72:535:411:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:test risk sharing by examining the response of consumption growth to income may have
15:580:36682:16:16:72:535:395:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:low power if income changes are (at least partly) anticipated by individuals. He instead
15:581:36770:16:16:72:535:379:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:proposed to use idiosyncratic events that are arguably harder to predict, such as plant
15:582:36857:16:16:72:535:363:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:closures, long strikes, long illnesses, and so on. Cochrane rejected full insurance for illness
15:583:36952:16:16:72:535:347:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:or involuntary job loss but not for long spells of unemployment, strikes or involuntary moves.
15:584:37046:16:16:72:535:331:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Notice that a crucial assumption in all of the work of this kind is that none of these shocks
15:585:37139:16:21:72:496:315:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can be correlated with unmeasured factors that determine marginal utility growth.
15:586:37220:21:16:89:538:294:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Townsend(1994)testedforrisksharinginvillageeconomiesofIndiaandconcludedthat
15:587:37295:16:15:72:535:278:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:although the model was statistically rejected, full insurance provided a surprisingly good
15:588:37385:15:16:72:535:263:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:benchmark. Specifically, he found that individual consumption comoves with village-level
15:589:37473:16:21:72:514:247:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumption and is not influenced much by own income, sickness, and unemployment.
15:590:37554:21:16:89:540:226:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Attanasio and Davis(1996)observethatequation(2)mustalsoholdformulti-year
15:591:37626:16:16:72:535:210:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:changes in consumption and when aggregated across groups of individuals.15This implies,
15:592:37713:16:16:72:535:194:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for example, that even if one group of individuals experience faster income growth relative
15:593:37804:16:21:72:535:178:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to another group during a ten year period, their consumption growth must be the same.
15:594:37889:21:9:72:532:157:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:implement (through taxes and transfers), the transfer of leisure is harder to defend on empirical grounds.
15:595:37995:9:15:81:534:148:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:14Because individual wages are measured with (often substantial) error in micro survey datasets, an OLS
15:596:38098:15:12:71:535:133:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:estimation of this regression would suffer from attenuation bias, which may lead to a failure to reject full
15:597:38206:12:12:71:535:121:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:insurance even when it is false. The papers discussed here employ different approaches to deal with this issue
15:598:38316:12:12:71:534:109:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:(such as using an Instrumental Variables regression or averaging across groups to average out measurement
15:599:38421:12:8:71:99:97:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:error).
15:600:38428:8:0:81:410:89:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:15Hayashi et al.(1996)alsousemulti-yearchangestotestforrisksharing.
16:601:38497:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The substantial rise in the education premium in the United States (i.e., the wages of
16:602:38583:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:college graduates relative to high school graduates) throughout the 1980’s provided a key
16:603:38672:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:test of perfect risk sharing. Contrary to this hypothesis, they found that the consumption
16:604:38762:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of college graduates grew much faster than that of high school graduates during the same
16:605:38850:16:21:72:339:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:period, violating the premise of perfect risk sharing.
16:606:38904:21:16:89:538:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Finally,Schulhofer-Wohl(2011)shedsnewlightonthisquestion. Hearguesthatifmore
16:607:38980:16:16:72:535:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:risk-tolerant individuals self-select into occupations with more (aggregate) income risk, then
16:608:39074:16:16:72:535:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the regressions in (3)usedbyCochrane(1991),Nelson(1994), and others (which incorrectly
16:609:39160:16:15:72:535:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:assumes away such correlation) will be biased towards rejecting perfect risk sharing. By
16:610:39248:15:16:72:535:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:using self-reported measures of risk attitudes from the Health and Retirement Survey, he
16:611:39336:16:16:72:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:establishes such a correlation.  Then he develops a method to deal with this bias and,
16:612:39422:16:16:72:535:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:applying the corrected regression, he finds that consumption growth responds very weakly
16:613:39510:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to idiosyncratic shocks, implying much larger risk sharing than found in these previous
16:614:39597:16:16:72:534:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:papers. He also shows that the coefficients estimated from this regression can be mapped
16:615:39685:16:30:72:261:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:into a measure of “partial insurance.”
16:616:39723:30:16:72:534:438:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Taking Stock.As the preceding discussion makes clear, with few exceptions, all em-
16:617:39805:16:16:72:535:422:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:pirical studies agree that perfect insurance in the whole population is strongly rejected in
16:618:39897:16:16:72:540:406:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:astatisticalsense. However,thisstatisticalrejectionperseisnotsufficienttoconclude
16:619:39978:16:16:72:534:390:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that complete markets is apoor benchmarkfor economic analysis for two reasons. First,
16:620:40063:16:16:72:535:374:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:there seem to be a fair deal of insurance against certain types of shocks, as documented by
16:621:40154:16:16:72:535:358:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Cochrane(1991)andTownsend(1994), and among certain groups of households, such as
16:622:40234:16:15:72:534:342:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in some villages in less developed countries (Townsend(1994)), or among non-stockholders
16:623:40322:15:16:72:534:327:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in the United States (Guvenen(2007a)). Second, the reviewed empirical evidence arguably
16:624:40409:16:16:72:535:311:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:documents statistical tests of an extreme benchmark (equation (1)) that we should not
16:625:40494:16:16:72:535:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:expect to hold precisely—for every household, against every shock.  Thus, with a large
16:626:40580:16:16:72:535:279:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:enough sample, statistical rejection should not be surprising.16What these tests do not do
16:627:40670:16:16:72:535:263:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is to tell us how “far” the economy is from the perfect insurance benchmark. In this sense,
16:628:40761:16:16:72:534:247:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:analyses such as inTownsend(1994)—that identify the types of shocks that are and are not
16:629:40849:16:16:72:534:231:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:insured—are somewhat more informative than those inAltug and Miller(1990),Hayashi
16:630:40930:16:16:71:539:215:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(1996), andGuvenen(2007a)thatrelyonmodelmisspecificationtypetestsofrisk
16:631:41007:16:34:71:111:199:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sharing.
16:632:41015:34:28:72:308:165:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:3.2  Benchmark 2: Self-Insurance
16:633:41047:28:16:72:535:137:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The rejection of full consumption insurance led economists to search for other benchmark
16:634:41135:16:18:72:535:121:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:frameworks for studying individual choices under uncertainty. One of the most influential
16:635:41224:18:16:81:534:103:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:16One view is that hypothesis tests without an explicit alternative (such as the ones discussed here) often
16:636:41331:16:0:71:490:87:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:“degenerate into elaborate rituals designed to measure the sample size. (Leamer(1983,p.39))”
17:637:41425:0:209:170:436:697:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Figure 1: Within-Cohort Inequality Over Life Cycle
17:638:41475:209:0:113:93:488:28:g_d0_f1:28:g_d0_f1:304050600.1

17:656:41577:0:239:358:470:673:34:Times:34:Times:Cross Sectional Variance of Log Consumption
17:657:41620:239:16:72:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:studies of this kind has beenDeaton and Paxson(1994), who brought a different kind
17:658:41702:16:16:72:535:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of evidence to bear. They began by documenting two empirical facts. Using micro data
17:659:41786:16:15:72:535:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from the United States, United Kingdom, and Taiwan, they first documented that within-
17:660:41872:15:16:72:535:387:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cohort inequality of labor income (as measured by the variance of log income) increases
17:661:41959:16:16:72:535:371:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:substantially and almost linearly over the life cycle. Second, they documented that within-
17:662:42050:16:16:72:535:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cohort consumption inequality showed a very similar pattern and also rose substantially as
17:663:42140:16:16:72:535:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuals age. The two empirical facts are replicated in figure1 from data inGuvenen
17:664:42226:16:21:71:150:323:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2007b, 2009a).
17:665:42241:21:16:89:535:302:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To understand what these patterns imply for the market structure, first consider a com-
17:666:42328:16:16:71:534:286:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:plete markets economy. As we saw in the previous section, if consumption is separable from
17:667:42418:16:16:71:534:270:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:leisure and other potential determinants of marginal utility, consumption growth will be
17:668:42506:16:15:71:535:254:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equalized across individuals, independent of any idiosyncratic shock (equation (2)). There-
17:669:42597:15:16:71:535:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fore, while consumption level may differ across individuals due to differences in permanent
17:670:42688:16:16:71:535:223:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lifetime resources, this dispersion shouldnotchange as the cohort ages.17Therefore,Deaton
17:671:42777:16:16:72:535:207:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and Paxson(1994)’s evidence has typically been interpreted as contradicting the complete
17:672:42865:16:16:72:308:191:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:markets framework. I now turn to the details.
17:673:42910:16:15:81:534:175:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:17There are two obvious modifications that preserve complete markets and would be consistent with rising
17:674:43014:15:12:71:534:160:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:consumption inequality. The first one is to introduce heterogeneity in time discounting. This is not very
17:675:43119:12:12:71:534:148:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:appealing because it “explains” by entirely relying on unobservable preference heterogeneity. Second, one
17:676:43224:12:12:71:534:136:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:could question the assumption of separability: if leisure is non-separable and wage inequality is rising over
17:677:43333:12:12:71:534:124:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:the life cycle—which it does—then consumption inequality would also rise to keep marginal utility growth
17:678:43437:12:12:71:534:112:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:constant (even under complete markets). But this explanation also predicts that hours inequality should
17:679:43540:12:12:71:535:100:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:also rise over the life cycle, a prediction that does not seem to be borne out in the data—although seeBadel
17:680:43648:12:0:71:368:88:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:and Huggett(2007)foraninterestingdissentingtakeonthispoint.
18:681:43709:0:29:72:293:696:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f20:3.2.1  The Permanent Income Model
18:682:43742:29:16:72:535:667:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The canonical framework for self-insurance is provided by the permanent income lifecycle
18:683:43830:16:16:72:535:651:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model, in which individuals have only access to a risk-free asset for borrowing and saving.
18:684:43921:16:15:72:535:635:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Therefore, as opposed to full insurance, there is only “self-insurance” in this framework.
18:685:44011:15:16:72:535:620:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Whereas the complete markets framework represents the maximum amount of insurance,
18:686:44093:16:16:72:535:604:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the permanent income model arguably provides the lower bound on insurance (to the extent
18:687:44181:16:16:72:535:588:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that we believe individuals have access to a savings technology, and borrowing is possible
18:688:44271:16:21:72:220:572:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:subject to some constraints).
18:689:44300:21:16:89:535:551:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:It is instructive to develop this framework in some detail as the resulting equations
18:690:44385:16:16:72:535:535:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:will come in handy in the subsequent exposition. The framework here closely followsHall

18:692:44550:15:29:71:243:504:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:permanent and transitory shocks:
18:693:44582:29:19:262:535:475:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:yt=yPt+"t,(4)

18:711:44878:16:16:71:535:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:problem can be solved in closed form to obtain a consumption function. First-differencing
18:712:44967:16:16:71:215:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this consumption rule yields

18:720:45031:13:17:211:535:216:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is the annuitization factor.18This term is close to zero when
18:721:45092:17:16:71:534:199:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the horizon is long and the interest rate is not too high, the well-understood implication
18:722:45182:16:16:71:535:183:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:being that the response of consumption to transitory shocks is very weak given their low

19:735:45855:34:16:89:535:633:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:So the rise in consumption inequality from aget-1totis a measure of the variance
19:736:45935:16:16:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the permanent shock between those two ages. Since, as seen in figure1,consumption
19:737:46019:16:16:72:535:601:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:inequality rises significantly and almost linearly, this figure is consistent with permanent

19:739:46199:46:16:72:535:539:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Deaton and Paxson’s Striking Conclusion.Based on this evidence,Deaton and Pax-
19:740:46277:16:16:72:540:523:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:son (1994)arguedthatthepermanentincomemodelisabetterbenchmarkforstudying
19:741:46349:16:16:72:539:507:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individual allocations than is complete markets.Storesletten et al.(2004b)wentonestep
19:742:46434:16:16:72:535:491:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:further and showed that a calibrated life cycle model with incomplete markets can be quan-
19:743:46524:16:16:72:535:475:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:titatively consistent with the rise in consumption inequality as long as income shocks are
19:744:46614:16:16:72:535:459:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sufficiently persistent (⇢&0.90). In his presidential address to the American Economic
19:745:46700:16:31:72:449:443:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Association, RobertLucas(2003, p. 10) succinctly summarized this view:
19:746:46770:31:15:118:505:412:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The fanning out over time of the earnings and consumption distributions
19:747:46841:15:16:101:506:397:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:within a cohort that Angus Deaton and Paxson (1994) document is striking
19:748:46913:16:31:101:465:381:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:evidence of a sizable, uninsurable random walk component in earnings.
19:749:46982:31:16:72:535:350:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This conclusion was shared by the bulk of the profession in the 1990’s and 2000’s, giving
19:750:47071:16:16:72:541:334:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:astrongimpetustothedevelopmentofincompletemarketsmodelsfeaturinglargeand
19:751:47143:16:16:72:536:318:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:persistent shocks that are uninsurable. I review many of these models in Sections 4 and 5.
19:752:47233:16:16:72:535:302:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:However, a number of recent papers have revisited the original Deaton-Paxson finding and
19:753:47321:16:27:72:253:286:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have reached a different conclusion.
19:754:47357:27:15:72:534:259:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Reassessing the Facts: An Opposite Conclusion.Four of these papers, by and large,
19:755:47438:15:16:72:535:244:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:follow the same methodology as described and implemented byDeaton and Paxson(1994),
19:756:47521:16:16:72:535:228:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:but each uses a data set that extends the original CE sample used by these authors (that
19:757:47609:16:16:72:535:212:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:covered 1980 to 1990) and differ somewhat in their sample selection strategy. Specifically,
19:758:47700:16:16:72:535:196:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Primiceri and van Rens(2009,figure2)usedatafrom1980to2000;Heathcote et al.(2010,
19:759:47780:16:16:72:538:180:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:figure 14) use the 1980 to 1998 sample;Guvenen and Smith(2009,figure11)usethe1980to
19:760:47863:16:16:72:538:164:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:1992 sample and augment it with the 1972-73 sample; andKaplan(2010,figure2)usesdata
19:761:47946:16:16:72:535:148:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from 1980 to 2003. WhereasDeaton and Paxson(1994,figures4and8)andStoresletten
19:762:48023:16:16:72:539:132:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(2004b,figure1)documentedariseinconsumptioninequalityofabout30logpoints
19:763:48100:16:0:72:535:116:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(between ages 25 and 65), these four papers find a much smaller rise of about 5–7 log points.
20:764:48195:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Taking Stock.Taken together, these reanalyses of CE data reveal thatDeaton and
20:765:48273:16:16:71:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Paxson(1994)’s earlier conclusion is not robust to small changes in the sample period
20:766:48358:16:16:71:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:studied. Although more work on this topic certainly seems warranted,19these recent studies
20:767:48448:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:raise substantial concerns on one of the key pieces of empirical evidence on the extent of
20:768:48538:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:market incompleteness. A small rise in consumption inequality is hard to reconcile with
20:769:48625:16:16:71:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the combination of large permanent shocksandself-insurance. Hence, if this latter view
20:770:48711:16:16:71:534:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is correct, either income shocks are not as permanent as we thought or there is insurance
20:771:48800:16:28:71:476:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:above and beyond self-insurance. Both of these possibilities are discussed next.
20:772:48880:28:27:72:391:556:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:3.3  An Intermediate Case: Partial Insurance
20:773:48924:27:15:72:539:529:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Anaturalintermediatecasetoconsiderisanenvironmentbetweenthetwoextremesoffull
20:774:49000:15:16:72:535:514:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:insurance and self insurance. That is, perhaps individuals have access to various sources
20:775:49089:16:16:72:534:498:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of insurance (e.g., through charities, help from family and relatives, etc.)in additionto
20:776:49178:16:16:72:535:482:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:borrowing and saving, but these forms of insurance still fall short of full insurance. If this
20:777:49272:16:19:72:506:466:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is the case, is there a way to properly measure the degree of this “partial insurance”?
20:778:49359:19:16:89:539:447:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To address this question,Blundell et al.(2008)examinetheresponseofconsumptionto

20:781:49605:16:29:72:420:399:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:parameters—✓and-—to encompass a variety of different scenarios:
20:782:49668:29:32:257:535:370:143:g_d0_f31:143:g_d0_f2:-ct=✓⌘t+--t"t.(7)
20:783:49685:32:16:89:535:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Now, at one extreme is the self-insurance model (i.e., the permanent income model):

20:792:50408:16:15:81:537:191:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:19For example, asAttanasio et al.(2007)showthatthefactsregardingtheriseinconsumptioninequality
20:793:50502:15:12:71:534:176:99:g_d0_f9:99:g_d0_f8:over timeare sensitive to whether one uses the “recall survey” or the “diary survey” in the CE dataset.
20:794:50605:12:12:71:534:164:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:All the papers discussed in this section (on consumption inequality over the life cycle, includingDeaton
20:795:50709:12:12:71:534:152:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:and Paxson(1994)) use the recall survey data. It would be interesting to see if the diary survey alters the
20:796:50816:12:9:71:351:140:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:conclusions regarding consumption inequality over the life cycle.
20:797:50881:9:15:81:535:131:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:20They also find--t=0.0533 (0.0435)indicating very small transmission of transitory shocks to con-
20:798:50979:15:9:72:493:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:sumption. This is less surprising since it would also be implied by the permanent income model.
