21:802:51309:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the maintained assumption inHall and Mishkin(1982)andDeaton and Paxson(1994).
21:803:51386:16:16:72:538:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Blundell et al.(2008)showthatonecanderive,asanapproximation,ananalogousequation
21:804:51465:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(7) with CRRA utility and self-insurance but now✓=-⇡⇡i,t, where⇡i,tis the ratio of
21:805:51547:16:16:71:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:human wealth to total wealth.  In other words, the coefficients✓and-are both equal
21:806:51629:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to 1 under self-insurance only if preferences are of quadratic form; generalizing to CRRA
21:807:51718:16:16:71:534:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:predicts that even with self insurance the response to permanent shocks, given by⇡i,t, will
21:808:51809:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:be less than one for one if non-human wealth is positive. Thus, accumulation of wealth
21:809:51895:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:due to precautionary savings or retirement can dampen the response of consumption to
21:810:51979:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:permanent shocks and give the appearance of partial insurance.Blundell et al.(2008)
21:811:52062:15:16:72:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:examine if younger individuals (who have less non-human wealth and thus have a higher
21:812:52147:16:16:72:534:537:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f2:⇡i,tthan older individuals) have a higher response coefficient to permanent shocks. They
21:813:52235:16:27:71:208:521:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:do find this to be the case.
21:814:52263:27:16:71:538:494:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Insurance or Advance Information?Primiceri and van Rens(2009)conductananal-
21:815:52338:16:16:71:540:478:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ysis similar toBlundell et al.(2008)andalsofindasmallresponseofconsumptionto
21:816:52414:16:16:72:534:462:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:permanent income movements.  However, they adopt a different interpretation for this
21:817:52498:16:16:72:535:446:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:finding—that income movements are largely “anticipated” by the individuals as opposed to
21:818:52586:16:15:72:535:430:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:being genuine permanent “shocks.” As has been observed as far back asHall and Mishkin
21:819:52671:15:16:72:535:415:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1982), this alternative interpretation illustrates a fundamental challenge with this kind of
21:820:52764:16:16:72:535:399:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:analysis: advance information and partial insurance are difficult to disentangle by simply
21:821:52854:16:27:72:331:383:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:examining the response of consumption to income.
21:822:52902:27:16:72:540:356:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Insurance or Less Persistent Shocks?Kaplan and Violante(2010)raisetwomore
21:823:52975:16:16:72:534:340:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:issues regarding the interpretation of✓. First, they ask, what if income shocks are per-
21:824:53063:16:16:72:535:324:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sistent but not permanent? This is a relevant question because, as I discuss in the next
21:825:53151:16:16:72:535:308:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:section, nearly all empirical studies that estimate the persistence coefficient (of an AR(1)
21:826:53243:16:15:72:535:292:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:or ARMA(1,1)) find it to be 0.95 or lower—sometimes as low as 0.7. To explore this is-
21:827:53329:15:16:72:535:277:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sue, they simulate data from a life cycle model with self insurance only, in which income
21:828:53418:16:16:72:535:261:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:shocks follow an AR(1) process with a first order autocorrelation of 0.95. They show that
21:829:53507:16:16:72:535:245:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:when they estimate✓as inBlundell et al.(2008), they find it to be close to the 2/3 figure
21:830:53596:16:16:71:535:229:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:reported by these authors.22Second, they add a retirement period to the lifecycle model,
21:831:53684:16:16:72:535:213:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which has the effect that now even a unit root shock is not permanent, given that its effect
21:832:53776:16:16:72:535:197:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:does not translate one for one into the retirement period. Thus, individuals have even more
21:833:53867:16:16:72:535:181:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:reason not to respond to permanent shocks, especially when they are closer to retirement.
21:834:53956:16:16:72:534:165:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Overall, their findings suggest that the response coefficient of consumption to income can
21:835:54046:16:17:72:536:149:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:be generated in a model of pure self-insurance to the extent that income shocks are allowed
21:836:54137:17:16:81:534:132:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:22The reason is simple. Because the AR(1) shock decays exponentially, this shock loses 5% of its value
21:837:54239:16:12:71:535:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:in one year, but1-0.9510⇡40%in 10 years and65%in 20 years. Thus, the discounted lifetime value of
21:838:54336:12:0:72:534:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:such a shock is significantly lower than a permanent shock which retains 100% of its value at all horizons.
22:839:54445:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to be slightly less than permanent.23One feature this model misses, however, is the age
22:840:54532:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:profile of response coefficients, which shows no clear trend in the data according toBlundell
22:841:54625:16:31:72:458:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(2008), but is upward sloping inKaplan and Violante(2010)’s model.
22:842:54697:31:15:72:535:633:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Taking Stock.Before the early 1990s, economists typically appealed to aggregation theo-
22:843:54784:15:16:72:535:618:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rems to justify the use of representative agent models. Starting in the 1990s, the widespread
22:844:54877:16:16:72:535:602:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rejections of the full insurance hypothesis (necessary forConstantinides(1982)’s theorem)
22:845:54966:16:16:72:539:586:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:combined with the findings ofDeaton and Paxson(1994)ledeconomiststoadoptversions
22:846:55046:16:16:72:535:570:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the permanent income model as a benchmark to study individual’s choices under uncer-
22:847:55133:16:16:72:534:554:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tainty (Hubbard et al.(1995),Carroll(1997),Carroll and Samwick(1997),Blundell and
22:848:55214:16:16:71:534:538:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Preston(1998),Attanasio et al.(1999),Gourinchas and Parker(2002), among many oth-
22:849:55295:16:16:71:534:522:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ers). The permanent income model has two key assumptions: a single risk-free asset for
22:850:55381:16:16:71:535:506:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:self-insuranceandpermanent—or very persistent—shocks, typically implying substantial
22:851:55465:16:15:71:534:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic risk. The more recent evidence, discussed in this subsection, however, sug-
22:852:55554:15:16:71:534:475:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:gests that a more appropriate benchmark needs to incorporate either more opportunities
22:853:55640:16:40:71:462:459:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for partial insurance or idiosyncratic risk that is smaller than once assumed.
22:854:55718:40:33:72:475:419:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:4IncompleteMarketsinGeneralEquilibrium
22:855:55756:33:16:72:535:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This section and the next discuss incomplete markets models in general equilibrium without
22:856:55846:16:16:72:535:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate shocks. Bringing in a general equilibrium structure allows researchers to jointly
22:857:55937:16:16:72:535:354:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:analyze aggregate and distributional issues. As we shall see, the two are often intertwined,
22:858:56029:16:16:72:535:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:making such models very useful.  The present section discusses the key ingredients that
22:859:56116:16:15:72:535:322:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:go into building a general equilibrium incomplete markets model (e.g., types of risks to
22:860:56204:15:16:72:535:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consider, borrowing limits, modeling individuals versus households, among others). The
22:861:56290:16:16:72:535:291:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:next section presents three broad questions that these models have been used to address: the
22:862:56382:16:16:72:535:275:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cross-sectional distributions of consumption, earnings, and wealth. These are substantively
22:863:56473:16:16:72:535:259:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:important questions and constitute an entry point into broader literatures. I now begin
22:864:56560:16:34:72:288:243:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with a description of the basic framework.
22:865:56602:34:29:72:297:209:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:4.1  The Aiyagari (1994) Model
22:866:56632:29:16:72:538:180:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In one of the first quantitative models with heterogeneity,Imrohoroglu(1989)constructeda
22:867:56720:16:16:72:535:164:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model with liquidity constraints and unemployment risk that varied over the business cycle.
22:868:56811:16:15:72:535:148:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:She assumed that interest rates were constant to avoid the difficulties with aggregate shocks,
22:869:56905:15:16:72:534:133:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which were subsequently solved byKrusell and Smith(1998). She used this framework to
22:870:56989:16:19:72:535:117:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:re-assessLucas(1987)’s earlier calculation of the welfare cost of business cycles. She found
22:871:57081:19:15:81:535:98:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:23Another situation in which✓<1with self-insurance alone is if permanent and transitory shocks are
22:872:57179:15:0:72:308:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:not separately observable and there is estimation risk.
23:873:57236:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:only a slightly higher figure than Lucas’, mainly because of her focus unemployment risk,
23:874:57325:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which typically has a short duration in the United States.24Regardless of its empirical
23:875:57412:16:21:72:465:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:conclusions, this paper represents an important early effort in this literature.
23:876:57492:21:16:89:539:643:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In what has become an important benchmark model,Aiyagari(1994)studiedaversion
23:877:57569:16:16:72:535:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the deterministic growth framework, with a Neoclassical production function and a large
23:878:57659:16:16:72:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:number of infinitely-lived consumers (dynasties).  Consumers are ex ante identical, but
23:879:57746:16:16:72:535:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:there is ex post heterogeneity due to idiosyncratic shocks to labor productivity which are
23:880:57836:16:16:72:535:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:not directly insurable (via insurance contracts).  However, consumers can accumulate a
23:881:57922:16:15:72:535:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(conditionally) risk-free asset for self insurance. They can also borrow in this asset, subject
23:882:58017:15:16:72:535:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to a limit determined in various ways. At each point in time, consumers may differ in the
23:883:58106:16:21:72:439:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:history of productivities experienced, and hence in accumulated wealth.
23:884:58177:21:38:89:396:511:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:More concretely, an individual solves the following problem:

23:896:58353:20:16:89:535:375:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:There are (at least) two ways to embed this problem in general equilibrium.Aiyagari
23:897:58436:16:16:71:539:359:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1994)consideredaproductioneconomyandviewedthesingleassetasthecapitalinthe
23:898:58510:16:16:71:534:343:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:firm, which obviously has a positive net supply. In this case, aggregate production is deter-
23:899:58603:16:16:71:538:327:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mined by the savings of individuals, and bothrand the wage ratew,mustbedeterminedin
23:900:58686:16:16:71:538:311:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:general equilibrium.Huggett(1993)insteadassumedthatthesingleassetwasahousehold
23:901:58764:16:16:71:535:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bond in zero net supply. In this case, the aggregate amount of goods in the economy is
23:902:58850:16:21:71:515:279:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:exogenous (exchange economy), and the only aggregate variable to be determined isr.
23:903:58933:21:16:89:535:258:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The borrowing limitBmincan be set to the “natural” limit, which is defined as the loosest
23:904:59022:16:15:72:541:242:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:possible constraint consistent with certain repayment of debt:Bmin=wlmin/r.Notethat
23:905:59105:15:16:72:535:227:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:iflminis zero, this natural limit will be zero. Some authors have used this feature to rule
23:906:59196:16:16:71:535:211:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:out borrowing (e.g.,Carroll(1997)andGourinchas and Parker(2002)). Alternatively, it
23:907:59279:16:16:71:487:195:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can be set to some ad hoc limit stricter than the natural one. More on this later.
23:908:59361:16:15:81:534:179:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:24There is a large literature on the costs of business cycles following Lucas’ original calculation. I do
23:909:59466:15:12:71:535:164:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:not discuss these papers here for brevity.Lucas(2003)’s presidential address to the American Economic
23:910:59567:12:12:71:534:152:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:Association is an extensive survey of this literature that also discusses how Lucas’ views on this issue evolved
23:911:59679:12:9:71:199:140:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:since the original 1987 paper.
23:912:59709:9:15:81:534:131:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:25Prior to Aiyagari, the decision problem described here was studied in various forms by, among others,
23:913:59812:15:12:71:535:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:Schechtman and Escudero(1977),Bewley(undated),Flavin(1981),Hall and Mishkin(1982),Clarida(1987,
23:914:59907:12:12:71:535:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:1990),Deaton(1991), andCarroll(1991). With the exceptions ofBewley(undated)andClarida(1987,
23:915:59998:12:12:71:534:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:1990), however, most of these earlier papers did not consider general equilibrium, which is the main focus
23:916:60104:12:0:71:92:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:here.
24:917:60111:0:16:89:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The main substantive finding inAiyagari(1994) is that with incomplete markets, the
24:918:60193:16:16:71:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate capital stock is higher than it is with complete markets, although the difference
24:919:60284:16:16:71:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is not quantitatively very large.  Consequently, the interest rate is lower (than the time
24:920:60374:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:preference rate), which is also true inHuggett(1993)’s exchange economy version. This
24:921:60459:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:latter finding initially led economists to conjecture that these models could help explain the
24:922:60553:16:16:71:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equity premium puzzle,26which is also generated by a low interest rate. It turned out that
24:923:60643:16:16:72:534:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:while this environment helps, it is neither necessary nor sufficient to generate a low interest
24:924:60738:16:16:72:534:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rate. I return to this issue later.Aiyagari(1994) also shows that the model generates the
24:925:60827:16:15:71:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:right ranking between different types of inequality: wealth is more dispersed than income,
24:926:60917:15:21:71:292:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which is more dispersed than consumption.
24:927:60958:21:16:89:540:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The frameworks analyzed byHuggett(1993)andAiyagari(1994)containthebare
24:928:61028:16:16:71:535:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bones of a canonical general equilibrium incomplete markets model.  As such, they ab-
24:929:61113:16:16:71:534:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stract from many ingredients that would be essential today for conducting serious empir-
24:930:61201:16:16:71:534:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ical/quantitative work, especially given that almost two decades have passed since their
24:931:61289:16:16:71:534:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:publication. In the next three subsections, I review three main directions the framework
24:932:61377:16:16:71:534:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can be extended. First, the nature of idiosyncratic risk is often crucial for the implications
24:933:61471:16:16:71:534:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:generated by the model. There is a fair bit of controversy about the precise nature and
24:934:61558:16:15:71:534:420:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:magnitude of such risks, which I discuss in some detail. Second, and as I alluded to above,
24:935:61649:15:16:71:534:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the treatment of borrowing constraints is very reduced form here. The recent literature has
24:936:61740:16:16:71:534:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:made significant progress in providing useful micro-foundations for a richer specification of
24:937:61833:16:16:71:534:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:borrowing limits. Third, the Huggett-Aiyagari model considers an economy populated by
24:938:61918:16:16:71:534:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bachelor(ette)s as opposed to families—this distinction clearly can have a big impact on
24:939:62006:16:41:71:293:341:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:economic decisions, which is also discussed.
24:940:62050:41:29:72:369:300:206:g_d0_f11:99:g_d0_f8:4.2  Nature of Idiosyncratic Income Risk27
24:941:62092:29:16:72:535:271:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The rejection of perfect insurance brought to the fore idiosyncratic shocks as important
24:942:62180:16:16:72:535:255:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:determinants of economic choices. However, after three decades of empirical research (since
24:943:62271:16:16:72:534:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Lillard and Willis(1978)), a consensus among researchers on the nature of labor income risk
24:944:62362:16:16:72:535:223:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:still remains elusive. In particular, the literature in the 1980s and 1990s produced two—
24:945:62451:16:17:72:535:207:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:quite opposite—views on the subject. To provide context, consider this general specification
24:946:62543:17:16:81:538:190:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:26The equity premium puzzle ofMehra and Prescott(1985)istheobservationthatinthehistoricaldata
24:947:62636:16:12:72:535:174:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:stocks yield a much higher return than bonds over long horizons, which has turned out to be very difficult
24:948:62742:12:8:72:279:162:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:to explain by a wide range of economic models.
24:949:62788:8:0:81:332:154:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:27The exposition here draws heavily onGuvenen(2009a).
25:950:62843:0:29:72:179:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for the wage process:
25:951:62864:29:8:113:247:667:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:yit=g(t,observables,...)
25:952:62888:8:10:147:246:659:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:|{z}
25:953:62892:10:0:139:255:649:64:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f4:common systematic component
25:954:62919:0:0:269:278:667:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f14:+
25:955:62920:0:9:305:310:676:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:⇥
25:956:62921:9:0:310:350:667:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f13:↵i+-it

25:958:62928:18:11:305:355:658:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:|{z}
25:959:62932:11:0:292:367:647:64:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f4:profile heterogeneity
25:960:62953:0:0:382:391:667:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f14:+

25:962:62955:9:0:427:460:667:143:g_d0_f13:64:g_d0_f15:zit+"it
25:963:62962:0:18:460:465:676:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:⇤
25:964:62963:18:0:422:465:658:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:|{z}
25:965:62967:0:20:465:468:667:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f13:,
25:966:62968:20:0:406:486:647:64:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f4:stochastic component
25:967:62988:0:37:520:535:667:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(9)
25:968:62991:37:29:113:535:630:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:zit=⇢zit-1+⌘it,(10)
25:969:63010:29:20:71:532:601:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:where⌘itand"itare zero mean innovations that are i.i.d. over time and across individuals.
25:970:63099:20:16:89:538:581:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The early papers on income dynamics estimated versions of the process given in (9)from
25:971:63185:16:16:71:535:565:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:labor income data and found:0.5<⇢<0.7,and-2--0(cf.,Lillard and Weiss(1979);
25:972:63260:16:16:72:535:549:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Hause(1980)).  Thus according to this first view, which I shall call the “Heterogeneous
25:973:63347:16:16:72:535:533:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Income Profiles” (HIP) model, individuals are subject to shocks with modest persistence,
25:974:63435:16:16:72:535:517:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:while facing life-cycle profiles that are individual-specific (and hence vary significantly across
25:975:63533:16:15:72:535:501:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the population).  As we will see in the next section, one theoretical motivation for this
25:976:63622:15:16:72:535:486:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:specification is the human capital model, which implies differences in income profiles if, for
25:977:63716:16:20:72:315:470:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:example, individuals differ in their ability level.
25:978:63767:20:16:89:540:450:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In an important paper,MaCurdy(1982)castdoubtonthesefindings. Hetestedthe
25:979:63839:16:16:72:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f14:null hypothesis of-2-=0and failed to reject it. He then proceeded by imposing-2-⌘0
25:980:63921:16:16:71:535:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:before estimating the process in (9), and found⇢⇡1(see alsoAbowd and Card(1989),
25:981:64001:16:16:72:534:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Topel(1990),Hubbard et al.(1995), andStoresletten et al.(2004a)). Therefore, according
25:982:64087:16:15:71:534:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to this alternative view, which I shall call the “Restricted Income Profiles” (RIP) model,
25:983:64177:15:16:71:534:371:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuals are subject to extremely persistent—nearly random walk—shocks, while facing
25:984:64264:16:29:71:237:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:similar life-cycle income profiles.
25:985:64299:29:16:71:535:326:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:MaCurdy (1982)’s Test.More recently, two papers have revived this debate.Baker
25:986:64377:16:16:71:535:310:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1997)andGuvenen(2009a) have shown that MaCurdy’s test has low power and therefore
25:987:64459:16:16:71:534:294:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the lack of rejection does not contain much information about whether or not there is growth
25:988:64551:16:16:71:534:278:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rate heterogeneity. MaCurdy’s test was generally regarded as the strongest evidence against
25:989:64642:16:15:71:535:262:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the HIP specification, and it was repeated in different forms by several subsequent papers
25:990:64732:15:16:71:535:247:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(Abowd and Card(1989); Topel(1990); andTopel and Ward(1992)), so it is useful to
25:991:64812:16:20:71:185:231:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discuss in some detail.
25:992:64835:20:16:89:534:211:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To understand its logic, notice that, using the specification in (9), thenthauto-covariance
25:993:64926:16:34:71:263:195:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of income growth can be shown to be
25:994:64961:34:0:197:343:161:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f17:cov(-yit,-yit+n)=-2--⇢n-1
25:995:64986:0:9:346:355:178:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:✓
25:996:64987:9:16:356:382:169:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f19:1-⇢
25:997:64990:16:0:356:382:153:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f19:1+⇢
25:998:64993:0:0:383:394:161:143:g_d0_f19:64:g_d0_f27:-2⌘
25:999:64996:0:17:395:404:178:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:◆
25:1000:64997:17:33:406:535:161:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:,(11)

25:1002:65088:16:16:71:535:112:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(due to exponential decay in⇢n-1), leaving behind a positive autocovariance equal to-2-.

26:1041:67093:16:16:71:534:138:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:sample size smaller than 500,000 observations (column 3)! Even in that case, only the18th
26:1042:67182:16:19:72:535:122:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:autocovariance is barely significant (with at-statistic of 1.67). For comparison,MaCurdy
26:1043:67270:19:15:81:535:103:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:28More concretely, the estimated value of-2-used in his Monte Carlo analysis implies that at age 55 more
26:1044:67374:15:0:71:330:88:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:than 70% of wage inequality is due to profile heterogeneity.
27:1045:67436:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1982)’s dataset included around 5,000 observations. Even the more recent PSID datasets
27:1046:67523:16:21:72:321:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:typically contain fewer than 40,000 observations.
27:1047:67572:21:16:89:535:659:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In light of these results, imposing theapriorirestriction of-2-=0on the estimation
27:1048:67654:16:16:72:535:643:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:exercise seems a risky route to follow.Baker(1997),Haider(2001),Haider and Solon
27:1049:67734:16:15:71:535:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2006), andGuvenen(2009a)estimatetheprocessin(9) without imposing this restriction
27:1050:67816:15:16:71:535:612:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and find substantial heterogeneity in-iand a low persistence, confirming the earlier results
27:1051:67908:16:16:72:539:596:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of Lillard and Weiss(1979)andHause(1980).Baker and Solon(2003)usealargepanel
27:1052:67984:16:16:72:535:580:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dataset drawn from Canadian tax records and allow for both permanent shocks and profile
27:1053:68071:16:21:72:472:564:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneity. They find statistically significant evidence of both components.
27:1054:68150:21:16:89:539:543:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In an interesting recent paper,Browning et al.(2010)estimateanincomeprocessthat
27:1055:68229:16:15:72:535:527:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:allows for “lots of” heterogeneity. The authors use a simulated method of moments estimator
27:1056:68320:15:16:72:535:512:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and match a number of moments whose economic significance is more immediate than the
27:1057:68404:16:16:72:535:496:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:covariance matrix of earnings residuals, which has typically been used as the basis of a
27:1058:68492:16:16:72:535:480:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:GMM estimation in the bulk of the extant literature. They uncover a lot of interesting
27:1059:68578:16:16:72:535:464:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneity, for example, in the innovation variance as well as in the persistence of AR(1)
27:1060:68671:16:16:72:535:448:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:shocks. Moreover, they “find strong evidence against the hypothesis that any worker has a
27:1061:68760:16:16:72:539:432:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:unit root.”Gustavsson and Osterholm(2010)usealongpaneldataset(1968-2005)from
27:1062:68836:16:16:72:535:416:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:administrative wage records on Swedish individuals. They employ local-to-unity techniques
27:1063:68925:16:29:72:428:400:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on individual-specific time series and reject the unit root assumption.
27:1064:68996:29:16:72:535:371:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Inferring Risk vs Heterogeneity from Economic Choices.Finally, a number of
27:1065:69070:16:16:72:535:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:recent papers examine the response of consumption to income shocks to infer the nature of
27:1066:69159:16:16:72:538:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:income risk. In an important paper,Cunha et al.(2005)measurethefractionofindividual-
27:1067:69243:16:16:72:535:323:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:specific returns to education that are predictable by individuals by the time they make their
27:1068:69336:16:16:72:535:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:college decision versus the part that represents uncertainty. Assuming a complete markets
27:1069:69425:16:16:72:535:291:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:structure, they find that slightly more than half of the returns to education represents
27:1070:69513:16:20:72:362:275:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:known heterogeneity from the perspective of individuals.
27:1071:69569:20:16:89:538:255:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Guvenen and Smith(2009)studythejointdynamicsofconsumptionandlaborincome
27:1072:69640:16:16:72:535:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(using PSID data) in order to disentangle “known heterogeneity” from income risk (coming
27:1073:69728:16:16:72:535:223:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from shocks as well from uncertainty regarding one’s own income growth rate).  They
27:1074:69811:16:16:72:535:207:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:conclude that a moderately persistent income process (⇢⇡0.7-0.8) is consistent with
27:1075:69894:16:16:72:535:191:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the joint dynamics of income and consumption. Furthermore, they find that individuals
27:1076:69979:16:16:72:535:175:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have significant information about their own-iat the time they enter the labor market
27:1077:70064:16:16:71:534:159:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and hence face little uncertainty coming from this component. Overall, they conclude that
27:1078:70153:16:15:71:534:143:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with income shocks of modest persistence and largely predictable income growth rates,
27:1079:70238:15:16:71:534:128:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the income risk perceived by individuals is substantially smaller than what is typically
27:1080:70326:16:16:71:534:112:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:assumed in calibrating incomplete markets models (many of which borrow their parameter
27:1081:70412:16:16:71:535:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:values fromMaCurdy(1982),Abowd and Card(1989), andMeghir and Pistaferri(2004),
27:1082:70490:16:0:72:540:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:among others).  Along the same lines,Krueger and Perri(2009)userichpaneldataon
28:1083:70570:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Italian households and conclude that the response of consumption to income suggests low
28:1084:70657:16:21:72:432:680:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:persistence for income shocks (or a high degree of partial insurance).29
28:1085:70729:21:16:89:535:659:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Studying economic choices to disentangle risk from heterogeneity has many advantages.
28:1086:70814:16:16:71:534:643:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Perhaps most importantly, it allows researchers to bring a much broader set of data to
28:1087:70900:16:16:71:535:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bear on the question. For example, many dynamic choices require individuals to carefully
28:1088:70988:16:16:71:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:weigh the different future risks they perceive against predictable changes before making a
28:1089:71078:16:16:71:534:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:commitment. Decisions on home purchases, fertility, college attendance, retirement savings,
28:1090:71169:16:16:71:534:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and so on are all of this sort. At the same time, this line of research also faces important
28:1091:71261:16:15:71:534:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:challenges: these analyses need to rely on a fully-specified economic model, so the results
28:1092:71352:15:16:71:534:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can be sensitive to assumptions regarding the market structure, specification of preferences,
28:1093:71445:16:16:71:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and so on. Therefore, experimenting with different assumptions is essential before a defini-
28:1094:71537:16:16:71:534:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tive conclusion can be reached with this approach. Overall, this represents a difficult but
28:1095:71628:16:34:71:318:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:potentially very fruitful area for future research.
28:1096:71679:34:29:72:346:466:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:4.3  Wealth, Health, and Other Shocks
28:1097:71716:29:16:72:535:437:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:One source of idiosyncratic risk that has received relatively little attention until recently
28:1098:71809:16:16:72:535:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:come from shocks to wealth holdings, resulting for example from fluctuations in housing
28:1099:71896:16:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:prices and stock returns, among others. A large fraction of the fluctuations in housing prices
28:1100:71990:16:15:72:535:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:are due to local or regional factors and are substantial (as the latest housing market crash
28:1101:72082:15:16:72:534:374:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:showed once again). So these fluctuations can have profound effects on individuals’ eco-
28:1102:72170:16:16:72:539:358:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nomic choices. In one recent example,Krueger and Perri(2009)usepaneldataonItalian
28:1103:72251:16:16:71:534:342:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:households’ income, consumption, and wealth. They study the response of consumption
28:1104:72334:16:16:71:534:326:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to income and wealth shocks and find the latter to be very important.  Similarly,Mian
28:1105:72419:16:16:71:539:310:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and Sufi(forthcoming)useindividual-leveldatafrom1997to2008andshowthathousing
28:1106:72495:16:16:71:534:294:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:price boom lead to significant equity extraction—about 25 cents for every dollar increase
28:1107:72584:16:16:71:534:278:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in prices—which in turn led to higher leverage and personal default during this time. Their
28:1108:72675:16:16:71:534:262:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:“conservative” estimates is that home equity-based borrowing added $1.25 trillion in house-
28:1109:72766:16:20:71:455:246:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:hold debt and accounted for about 40% of new defaults from 2006 to 2008.
28:1110:72838:20:16:89:535:226:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Another source of idiosyncratic shocks is out-of-pocket medical expenditures (hospi-
28:1111:72922:16:16:71:534:210:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tal bills, nursing home expenses, medications, etc), which can potentially have significant
28:1112:73013:16:16:71:539:194:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:effects on household decisions.French and Jones(2004)estimateastochasticprocessfor
28:1113:73095:16:16:71:534:178:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:health expenditures, modeled as a normal distribution adjusted to capture the risk of catas-
28:1114:73187:16:16:71:534:162:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:trophic health care costs. Simulating this process, they show that 0.1% of households every
28:1115:73278:16:18:71:534:146:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:year receive a health cost shock with a present value exceeding $125,000.Hubbard et al.
28:1116:73365:18:15:81:539:128:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:29Anumberofimportantpapershavealsostudiedtheresponseofconsumptiontoincome,suchas
28:1117:73445:15:12:71:535:113:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:Blundell and Preston(1998)andBlundell et al.(2008). These studies however assumed the persistence of
28:1118:73545:12:12:71:534:101:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:income shocks to be constant and instead focused on what can be learned about the sizes of income shocks
28:1119:73649:12:0:71:114:89:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:over time.
29:1120:73661:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1994,1995) represent the earliest efforts to introduce such shocks into quantitative in-
29:1121:73750:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:complete markets models. The 1995 paper shows that the interaction of such shocks with
29:1122:73836:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:means-tested social insurance programs are especially important to account for in order to
29:1123:73926:16:21:72:398:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:understand the very low savings rate of low-income individuals.
29:1124:73989:21:16:89:538:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:De Nardi et al.(2010)askiftheriskoflargeout-of-pocketmedicalexpenditureslatein
29:1125:74067:16:16:72:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:life can explain the savings behavior of the elderly. They examine a new and rich dataset
29:1126:74156:16:16:72:535:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:called AHEAD, which is part of the Health and Retirement Survey (HRS) conducted by the
29:1127:74242:16:16:72:535:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:University of Michigan, which allows them to characterize medical expenditure risk for the
29:1128:74332:16:15:72:535:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:elderly (even for those in their 90’s) more precisely than previous studies, such asHubbard
29:1129:74423:15:16:72:535:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(1995)andPalumbo(1999).30De Nardi et al. find out-of-pocket expenditures to rise
29:1130:74509:16:16:72:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dramatically at very old ages, which (in their estimated model) provides an explanation for
29:1131:74600:16:16:72:534:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the lack of significant dissaving by the elderly.Ozkan(2010) shows that the lifecycle profile
29:1132:74693:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of medical costs (inclusive of the costs paid by private and public insurers to providers)
29:1133:74783:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:differ significantly between rich and poor households. In particular, on average, the medical
29:1134:74876:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:expenses of the rich are higher than that of the poor until mid-life, after which the expenses
29:1135:74970:16:16:72:535:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the poor exceed those of the rich—by 25% in absolute terms. Further, the expenses of the
29:1136:75061:16:16:72:535:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:poor have thick tails—lots of individuals with zero expenses and many with catastrophically
29:1137:75152:16:15:72:535:420:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:high costs. He builds a model in which individuals can invest in their health (i.e., preventive
29:1138:75247:15:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:care), which affects the future distribution of health shocks and, consequently, the expected
29:1139:75340:16:16:72:535:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:life time. High-income individuals do precisely this, which explains their higher spending
29:1140:75430:16:16:72:535:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:early on. Low-income individuals do the opposite, which ends up costing more later in life.
29:1141:75521:16:16:72:535:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:He concludes that a reform of the health care system that encourages use of health care
29:1142:75608:16:16:72:535:341:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for low-income individuals have positive welfare gains, even when fully accounting for the
29:1143:75698:16:41:72:290:325:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:increase in taxes required to pay for them.
29:1144:75741:41:29:72:334:284:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:4.4  Endogenizing Credit Constraints
29:1145:75777:29:16:72:535:255:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The basic Aiyagari model features a reduced-form specification for borrowing constraints
29:1146:75865:16:16:72:535:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(8), and does not model the lenders’ problem that gives rise to such constraint. As such, it
29:1147:75957:16:16:72:535:223:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is silent about potentially interesting variation in borrowing limits across individuals and
29:1148:76049:16:20:72:463:207:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:states of the economy. A number of recent papers attempt to close this gap.
29:1149:76124:20:16:89:540:187:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In one of the earliest studies of this kind,Athreya(2002)constructedageneralequi-
29:1150:76205:16:18:72:535:171:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:librium model of unsecured household borrowing to quantify the welfare effects of the
29:1151:76290:18:16:81:534:153:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:30Palumbo’s estimates of medical expenditures is quite a bit smaller than that inDe Nardi et al.(2010),
29:1152:76393:16:12:72:537:137:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:which is largely responsible for the smaller effects he quantifies.De Nardi et al.(2010)arguethatonereason
29:1153:76499:12:12:72:535:125:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:for the discrepancy could be the fact that Palumbo used data from the National Medical Care Expenditure
29:1154:76602:12:12:72:535:113:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:Survey, which, unlike the AHEAD dataset, does not contain direct measures of nursing home expenses.
29:1155:76701:12:12:72:535:101:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:He did imputations from a variety of sources, which may be missing the large actual magnitude of such
29:1156:76802:12:0:72:244:89:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:expenses found in the AHEAD dataset.
30:1157:76840:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy Reform Act of 1999 in the United States. In thepoolingequilibrium of this
30:1158:76924:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model (which is what Athreya focused on), the competitive lending sector charges a higher
30:1159:77013:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:borrowing rate than the market lending rate to break even (i.e., zero profit condition), ac-
30:1160:77105:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:counting for the fraction of households who will default. This framework allows him to study
30:1161:77197:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:different policies, such as changing the stringency of means testing as well as eliminating
30:1162:77288:16:21:72:189:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy altogether.
30:1163:77310:21:16:89:539:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In an important paper,Chatterjee et al.(2007)buildamodelofpersonaldefaultbe-
30:1164:77386:16:16:72:535:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:havior and endogenous borrowing limits. The model features (i) several types of shocks—to
30:1165:77475:16:15:72:535:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:earnings, preferences, and liabilities (e.g., hospital and lawsuit bills, which precede a large
30:1166:77570:15:16:72:535:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fraction of defaults in the United States), (ii) a competitive banking sector, and (iii) post-
30:1167:77664:16:16:72:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy legal treatment of defaulters that mimics the US Chapter 7 bankruptcy code.
30:1168:77750:16:16:72:535:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The main contribution ofChatterjee et al.(2007)istoshowthataseparatingequilibrium
30:1169:77831:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:exist in which banks offer amenuof debt contracts to households whose interest rate varies
30:1170:77921:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:optimally with the level of borrowing to account for the changing default probability. Us-
30:1171:78011:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ing a calibrated version of the model, they quantify the separate contributions of earnings,
30:1172:78103:16:16:72:539:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:preferences, and liability shocks to debt and default.Chatterjee and Eyigungor(2011)in-
30:1173:78190:16:15:72:535:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:troduce collateralized debt (i.e., mortgage debt) into this framework to examine the causes
30:1174:78281:15:21:72:418:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the run-up in foreclosures and crash in housing prices after 2007.
30:1175:78350:21:16:89:540:400:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Livshits et al.(2007)studyamodelsimilartoChatterjee et al.(2007)inorderto
30:1176:78423:16:16:72:535:384:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:quantify the advantages to a “fresh start” bankruptcy system (e.g., US Chapter 7) against
30:1177:78512:16:16:72:535:368:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:a European style system in which debtors cannot fully discharge their debt in bankruptcy.
30:1178:78601:16:16:72:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The key trade-offis that dischargeable debts adds insurance against bad shocks, helping to
30:1179:78691:16:16:72:535:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:smooth across states, but the inability to commit to future repayment increase interest rates
30:1180:78784:16:16:72:535:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and limits the ability to smooth across time. Their model is quite similar toChatterjee et al.
30:1181:78878:16:16:72:535:304:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2007), except that they model an explicit OLG structure. They calibrate the model to the
30:1182:78967:16:15:72:535:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:age-specific bankruptcy rate and debt-to-earnings ratio. For their baseline parameterization,
30:1183:79060:15:16:72:535:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:they find that fresh start bankruptcy is welfare improving, but that result is sensitive to the
30:1184:79155:16:16:72:535:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:process for expenditure and income shocks, the shape of the earnings profile and household
30:1185:79245:16:16:72:539:241:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:size.Livshits et al.(2010)buildonthisframeworktoevaluateseveraltheoriesfortherise
30:1186:79326:16:16:72:539:225:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in personal bankruptcies since the 1970s. Finally,Glover and Short(2010)usethemodel
30:1187:79409:16:16:72:535:209:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of personal bankruptcy to understand the incorporation of entrepreneurs. Incorporation
30:1188:79495:16:16:72:535:193:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:protects the owners’ personal assets and their access to credit markets in case of default,
30:1189:79586:16:16:72:535:177:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:but by increasing their likelihood of default, incorporation also implies a risk premium is
30:1190:79677:16:34:72:230:161:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:built into their borrowing rate.
30:1191:79709:34:29:72:335:127:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:4.5  From Bachelor(ette)s to Families
30:1192:79746:29:15:72:535:98:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:While the framework described above can shed light on some interesting distributional
30:1193:79831:15:0:72:535:83:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:issues (e.g., inequality in consumption, earnings, and wealth), it is completely silent on
31:1194:79923:0:16:72:540:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:acrucialsourceofheterogeneity—thehouseholdstructure. Inreality,individualsmarry,
31:1195:80003:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:divorce, have kids and make their decisions regarding consumption, savings, labor supply
31:1196:80091:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and so on, jointly with these other life choices. For many economic and policy questions, the
31:1197:80184:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:interaction between these domestic decisions and economic choices in an incomplete markets
31:1198:80274:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:world can have a first order effect on the answers we get. Just to give a few example, consider
31:1199:80369:16:16:72:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:these facts: men and women are well-known to exhibit different labor supply elasticities;
31:1200:80458:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the tax treatment of income varies depending on whether an individual is single, married,
31:1201:80547:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and whether he/she have kids, etc.; the trends in labor market participation rate in the
31:1202:80635:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:United States since the 1960s have been markedly different for single and married women;
31:1203:80723:15:16:72:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the fractions of individuals who are married and divorced have changed significantly, again
31:1204:80814:16:21:72:209:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:since the 1960s, and so on.
31:1205:80841:21:16:89:540:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Aburgeoningliteratureworkstobringaricherhouseholdstructureintomacroeco-
31:1206:80912:16:16:72:540:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nomics.  For example, in an influential paperGreenwood et al.(2005)studytheroleof
31:1207:80993:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:household technologies (the widespread availability of washing machines, vacuum cleaners,
31:1208:81082:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:refrigerators, etc.) in leading women into the labor market.Greenwood and Guner(2008)
31:1209:81167:16:16:72:535:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:extend the analysis to study the marriage and divorce patterns since World War II.Jones et
31:1210:81257:16:15:72:548:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:al.  (2003)exploretheroleoftheclosinggenderwagegapformarriedwomen’srisinglabor
31:1211:81335:15:16:72:535:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:supply.Knowles(2007) argues that the working hours of men are too long when viewed
31:1212:81417:16:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:through the lens of a unitary model of the household in which the average wage of females
31:1213:81506:16:16:72:535:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rise as in the data. He shows that introducing bargaining between spouses into the model
31:1214:81594:16:16:72:535:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:reconciles it with the data.Guner et al.(2010) study the effects of potential reforms in
31:1215:81682:16:16:72:535:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the US tax system in a model of families with children and an extensive margin for female
31:1216:81771:16:16:72:538:341:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:labor supply.Guvenen and Rendall(2011)studytheinsuranceroleofeducationforwomen
31:1217:81849:16:16:72:535:325:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:against divorce risk and the joint evolution of education trends with those in marriage and
31:1218:81940:16:36:72:112:309:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:divorce.
31:1219:81948:36:33:72:525:273:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:5InequalityinConsumption,Wealth,andEarnings
31:1220:81991:33:16:72:539:240:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Amajoruseofheterogeneous-agentmodelsistostudyinequalityordispersioninkeyeco-
31:1221:82067:16:16:72:535:224:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nomic outcomes, most notably in consumption, earnings, and wealth. The Aiyagari model—
31:1222:82153:16:15:72:535:208:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as well as its aggregate-shock augmented version, the Krusell-Smith model presented in the
31:1223:82243:15:16:72:535:193:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:next section—takes earnings dispersion to be exogenous and makes predictions about in-
31:1224:82329:16:16:72:535:177:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equality in consumption and wealth. The bulk of the incomplete markets literature follows
31:1225:82418:16:16:72:535:161:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this lead in their analysis. Some studies introduce an endogenous labor supply choice and
31:1226:82507:16:16:72:535:145:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:instead specify the wage process to be exogenous, delivering earnings dispersion as an en-
31:1227:82597:16:16:72:535:129:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dogenous outcome (Pijoan-Mas(2006),Domeij and Floden(2006),Heathcote et al.(2008),
31:1228:82679:16:16:71:534:113:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:among others). While this is a useful step forward, a lot of the dispersion in earnings before
31:1229:82773:16:16:71:534:97:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:age 55 is due to wages and not hours, so the assumption of an exogenous wage process
31:1230:82857:16:0:71:534:81:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:still leaves quite a bit to be understood. Other strands of the literature attempt to close
32:1231:82950:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this gap by writing models that also generate wage dispersion as an endogenous outcome in
32:1232:83039:16:16:72:534:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the model—for example, due to human capital accumulation (e.g.,Guvenen and Kuruscu
32:1233:83121:16:34:72:495:664:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:(2009,forthcoming), andHuggett et al.(forthcoming)) or due to search frictions.31
32:1234:83202:34:29:72:275:630:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:5.1  Consumption Inequality
32:1235:83229:29:16:72:535:601:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Two different dimensions of consumption inequality has received attention in the literature.
32:1236:83321:16:16:72:535:585:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The first one concerns how much within-cohort consumption inequality increases over the
32:1237:83408:16:16:72:535:569:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lifecycle. The different views on this question has been summarized in Section3.2  .32The
32:1238:83497:16:16:71:534:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:second one concerns whether, and by how much, (overall) consumption inequality has risen
32:1239:83585:16:15:71:534:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in the United States since the 1970s, a question whose urgency was raised by the substantial
32:1240:83677:15:16:71:534:522:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rise in wage inequality during the same time. In one of the earliest papers on this topic,
32:1241:83767:16:16:71:535:506:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Cutler and Katz(1992) used data from the 1980s on US households from the Consumer
32:1242:83848:16:16:71:534:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Expenditure Survey (CE) and found that the evolution of consumption inequality closely
32:1243:83934:16:16:71:534:474:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tracked the rise in wage inequality during the same time. This finding served as a rejection
32:1244:84026:16:16:71:535:458:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of earlier claims in the literature (e.g.,Jencks(1984)) that the rise of means tested in-
32:1245:84115:16:16:71:534:442:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:kind transfers starting in the 1970s had improved the material well-being of low income
32:1246:84202:16:21:71:436:426:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:households relative to what would be judged by their income statistics.
32:1247:84273:21:16:89:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Interest in this question was reignited more recently by a thought-provoking paper by
32:1248:84358:16:15:71:534:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Krueger and Perri(2006), who concluded from an analysis of CE data that, from 1980 to
32:1249:84443:15:16:71:535:374:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:2003,within-groupincome inequality increased substantially more than within-group con-
32:1250:84529:16:16:71:535:358:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sumption inequality (in contrast, they found thatbetween-groupincome and consumption
32:1251:84613:16:16:71:535:342:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:inequality tracked each other).33They then proposed an explanation based on the premise
32:1252:84700:16:16:72:535:326:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that the development of financial services in the US economy has helped households smooth
32:1253:84789:16:21:72:349:310:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumption fluctuations relative to income variation.
32:1254:84843:21:16:89:534:289:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To investigate this story, they applied a model of endogenous debt constraints as in
32:1255:84927:16:16:72:534:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Kehoe and Levine(1993).  In this class of models, what is central is not the ability of
32:1256:85014:16:18:72:535:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:households to pay back their debt, but rather it is their incentives or willingness to pay
32:1257:85104:18:15:81:534:239:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:31The search literature is very large with many interesting models to cover. I do not discuss these models
32:1258:85210:15:12:71:534:224:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:here because I cannot do justice to this extensive body of work in this limited space. For an excellent survey,
32:1259:85321:12:12:71:534:212:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:see Rogerson et al.(2005). Note, however, that asHornstein et al.(forthcoming) show, search models have
32:1260:85424:12:8:72:409:200:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:trouble generating the magnitudes of wage dispersion we observe in the data.
32:1261:85500:8:16:81:535:192:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:32Another recent paper is of interest isAguiar and Hurst(2008), who examine the lifecycle mean and
32:1262:85598:16:12:71:534:176:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:variance profiles of the subcomponents of consumption—housing, utility bills, clothing, food at home, food
32:1263:85704:12:12:71:534:164:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:away from home, etc.  They show rich patterns that vary across categories, whereby the variance rises
32:1264:85805:12:12:71:534:152:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:monotonically for some categories, while being hump-shaped for others, and yet declining monotonically
32:1265:85907:12:12:71:534:140:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:for some others. The same patterns are observed for the mean profile. These disaggregated facts provide
32:1266:86010:12:8:71:233:128:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:more food for thought to researchers.
32:1267:86047:8:16:81:535:120:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:33Attanasio et al.(2007) have questioned the use of the CE Interview survey and argued that some
32:1268:86143:16:12:72:535:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:expenditure items are poorly measured in the survey relative to another component of CE, called the
32:1269:86242:12:12:72:535:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:diary survey. They propose an optimal way of combining the two survey data and find that consumption
32:1270:86342:12:0:72:535:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:inequality, especially in the 1990s has increased more than what is revealed by the Interview survey alone.
33:1271:86451:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:back. To give the right incentives, lenders can punish a borrower that defaults, for example,
33:1272:86544:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by banning her from financial markets forever (autarky). However, if the individual borrows
33:1273:86635:16:16:72:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:too much or if autarky is not sufficiently costly, it may still make sense to default in certain
33:1274:86731:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:states of the world. Thus, given the parameters of the economic environment, lenders will
33:1275:86820:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:compute the optimal state-contingent debt limit, which will ensure that the borrower never
33:1276:86910:16:16:72:539:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:defaults in equilibrium.Krueger and Perri(2006)noticethatifincomeshocksarereally
33:1277:86990:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:volatile, then autarky is a really bad outcome, giving borrowers less incentive to default.
33:1278:87081:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Lenders who know this, in turn, are more willing to lend, which endogenously loosens the
33:1279:87169:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:borrowing constraints. This view of the last 30 years thus holds that the rise in the volatility
33:1280:87265:15:16:72:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of income shocks gave rise to the development of financial markets (more generous lending),
33:1281:87356:16:21:72:393:537:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:which in turn led to a smaller rise in consumption inequality.34
33:1282:87420:21:16:89:540:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Heathcote et al.(2007)arguethatthesmallriseinconsumptioninequalitycanbe
33:1283:87491:16:16:71:534:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:explained simply if the rise in income shocks have been of more transitory nature, since such
33:1284:87584:16:16:71:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:shocks are easier to smooth through self insurance. Indeed,Blundell and Preston(1998)
33:1285:87669:16:16:71:534:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:earlier made the same observation to conclude that in the 1980s the rise in income shock
33:1286:87757:16:16:71:534:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:variance was mostly permanent in nature (evidenced by the observation that income and
33:1287:87842:16:16:71:534:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumption inequality grew together) whereas in the 1990s, it was mostly transitory given
33:1288:87932:16:15:71:539:420:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the opposite was true.Heathcote et al.(2007)calibrateafullyspecifiedmodelandshow
33:1289:88012:15:16:71:534:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that it can go a long way towards explaining the observed trends in consumption inequality.
33:1290:88103:16:16:71:534:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:One point to keep in mind is that that these papers take as given that the volatility of
33:1291:88191:16:16:71:534:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:income shocks rose during this period, a conclusion that is subject to uncertainty in light
33:1292:88282:16:21:71:259:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the new evidence discussed above.
33:1293:88318:21:16:89:535:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Before concluding, a word of caution about measurement. The appropriate price deflator
33:1294:88404:16:16:71:535:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for consumption may have trended differently for households in different parts of the income
33:1295:88496:16:16:71:535:304:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:distribution (i.e., the “Walmart effect” at the lower end). To the extent that this effect is
33:1296:88589:16:15:71:534:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:real, the measured trend in consumption inequality could be overstating the actual rise in
33:1297:88679:15:35:71:490:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the dispersion of material well-being. This issue still deserves a fuller exploration.
33:1298:88765:35:28:72:232:238:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:5.2  Wealth Inequality
33:1299:88787:28:16:72:535:210:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The main question about wealth inequality is a cross-sectional one: Why do we observe
33:1300:88872:16:16:72:535:194:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:such enormous disparities in wealth, with a Gini coefficient of about 0.8 for net worth and
33:1301:88963:16:21:72:293:178:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aGiniexceeding0.90forfinancialwealth?
33:1302:89000:21:16:89:535:157:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Economists have developed several models that can generate highly skewed wealth dis-
33:1303:89084:16:18:72:535:141:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tributions (see, for example,Huggett(1996),Krusell and Smith(1998),Quadrini(2000),
33:1304:89166:18:16:81:538:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:34Very recently,Aguiar and Bils(2011)havetakenadifferentapproachandconstructedameasureof
33:1305:89254:16:12:72:535:107:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:CE consumption by using data on income and (self-reported) savings rate by households.  They argue
33:1306:89352:12:12:72:535:95:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:that consumption inequality tracked income inequality closely in the past 30 years. Although this is still
33:1307:89458:12:0:72:345:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:preliminary work, the paper raises some interesting challenges.
34:1308:89523:0:16:72:534:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Castañeda et al.(2003),Guvenen(2006), andCagetti and De Nardi(2006). These models
34:1309:89604:16:16:71:534:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:typically use one (or more) of three mechanisms to produce this inequality: (1) dispersion
34:1310:89694:16:16:71:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in luck in the form of large and persistent shocks to labor productivity: the rich are luckier
34:1311:89788:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:than the poor; (2) dispersion in patience or thriftiness: the rich save more than the poor;
34:1312:89879:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and (3) dispersion in rates of return: the rich face higher asset returns than the poor. This
34:1313:89972:16:16:71:534:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:section describes a baseline model and variations of it that incorporate various combinations
34:1314:90065:16:16:71:534:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the three main mechanisms that economists have used to generate substantial inequality
34:1315:90154:16:29:71:234:584:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:in general equilibrium models.35
34:1316:90186:29:16:72:541:555:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Dispersion in Luck.Huggett(1996)askshowmuchprogresscanbemadetowards
34:1317:90253:16:16:71:534:539:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:understanding wealth inequality using (i) a standard lifecycle model with (ii) Markovian
34:1318:90341:16:16:71:534:523:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic shocks, (iii) uncertain lifetimes and (iv) a Social Security system. He finds
34:1319:90432:16:15:71:535:507:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that although the model can match the Gini coefficient for wealth in the United States,
34:1320:90519:15:16:71:534:492:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this comes from low income households holding too little wealth, rather than the extreme
34:1321:90607:16:16:71:534:476:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:concentration of wealth at the top in the US economy. Moreover, whereas in the US data the
34:1322:90697:16:16:71:534:460:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dispersion of wealth within each cohort is nearly as large as the dispersion across cohorts,
34:1323:90789:16:20:71:309:444:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the model understates the former significantly.
34:1324:90836:20:16:89:535:424:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Castañeda et al.(2003)studyanenrichedmodelthatcombineselementsofAiyagari
34:1325:90908:16:16:71:535:408:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1994)andHuggett(1996). Specifically, the model (i) has a Social Security system, (ii)
34:1326:90994:16:16:71:534:392:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:has perfectly altruistic bequests, (iii) allows for intergenerational correlation of earnings
34:1327:91087:16:16:71:534:376:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ability, (iv) has a progressive labor and estate tax system as in the US, and (iv) allows a
34:1328:91178:16:16:71:534:360:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:labor supply decision. As for the stochastic process for earnings, they do not calibrate its
34:1329:91270:16:15:71:534:344:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:properties based on micro-econometric evidence on income dynamics as is commonly done,
34:1330:91356:15:16:71:535:329:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:but rather they choose its features (the4⇥4transition matrix and 4 states of a Markov
34:1331:91441:16:16:71:534:313:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:process) so that the model matches the cross-sectional distribution of earnings and wealth.
34:1332:91532:16:16:71:533:297:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:To match the extreme concentration of wealth at the upper tail, this calibration procedure
34:1333:91622:16:16:71:534:281:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:implies that individuals must receive a large positive shock (about 1060 times the median
34:1334:91711:16:16:71:534:265:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:income level) with a small probability. This high income level is also very fleeting—it lasts
34:1335:91804:16:16:71:534:249:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for about 5 years—which leads these high income individuals to save substantially (for
34:1336:91890:16:29:71:391:233:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consumption smoothing) and results in high wealth inequality.
34:1337:91951:29:16:71:535:204:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Dispersion in Patience.Laitner(1992,2002)’s original insight was that wealth inequal-
34:1338:92036:16:16:71:534:188:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ity could result from a combination of: (1) random heterogeneity in lifetime incomes across
34:1339:92127:16:16:71:534:172:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:generations, and (2) altruistic bequests, which are constrained to be non-negative. Each
34:1340:92215:16:16:71:534:156:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:newly born consumer in Laitner’s model receives a permanent shock to his lifetime income
34:1341:92303:16:15:71:534:140:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and, unlike in the Aiyagari model, faces no further shocks to income during his lifetime. In
34:1342:92395:15:18:71:534:125:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:essence, in Laitner’s model only households who earn higher than average lifetime income
34:1343:92483:18:15:81:534:107:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:35Some of the models discussed in this section contain aggregate shocks in addition to idiosyncratic ones.
34:1344:92589:15:12:71:534:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:While aggregate shocks raise some technical issues that will be addressed in the next section, they pose no
34:1345:92696:12:0:71:257:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:problems for the exposition in this section.
35:1346:92742:0:178:138:468:697:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Figure 2: Determination of Wealth Inequality in Various Models
