35:1369:93084:0:114:509:510:661:25:Times:25:Times: 
35:1370:93084:114:7:386:504:547:25:Times:25:Times:Nonstockholders’     wealthStockholders’
35:1371:93124:7:0:476:495:540:25:Times:25:Times:     wealth
35:1372:93135:0:7:362:366:625:25:Times:14:Times:Rs
35:1373:93137:7:100:362:366:618:25:Times:14:Times:Rf
35:1374:93139:100:0:338:350:518:25:g_d0_f46:14:Times:−Bmin
35:1375:93144:0:7:435:506:654:25:Times:25:Times:Long−Run Asset Demand Schedule
35:1376:93174:7:146:435:347:647:25:g_d0_f51:31:g_d0_f51:η: Time preference rateη
35:1377:93198:146:35:370:456:501:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:(b)   Guvenen(2006)
35:1378:93217:35:16:72:535:466:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:want to transfer some amount to their offsprings who are not likely to be as fortunate. This
35:1379:93309:16:16:72:535:450:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:altruistic motive makes these households effectively more thrifty (compared to those who
35:1380:93397:16:16:72:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:earn below average income) since they also care about future utility. Thus even small dif-
35:1381:93487:16:16:72:535:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ferences in lifetime income can result in large differences in savings rates—a fact empirically
35:1382:93582:16:21:72:415:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:documented byCarroll(2000)—and hence in wealth accumulation.
35:1383:93642:21:15:89:539:381:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The stochastic-beta model ofKrusell and Smith(1998)isavariationonthisideaina
35:1384:93718:15:16:72:535:366:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dynastic framework, where heterogeneity in thrift (i.e., in the time-discount rate) is imposed
35:1385:93812:16:16:72:534:350:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:exogenously.36Being more parsimonious, the stochastic-beta model also allows for the
35:1386:93896:16:16:72:535:334:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:introduction of aggregate shocks. Krusell and Smith show that even small differences in
35:1387:93983:16:16:72:534:318:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the time discount factor that are sufficiently persistent is sufficient to generate the extreme
35:1388:94078:16:16:72:535:302:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:skewness of the US wealth distribution. The intuition for this result will be discussed in a
35:1389:94170:16:27:72:117:286:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:moment.
35:1390:94177:27:16:72:535:259:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Dispersion in Rates of Return.Guvenen(2006) introduces return differentials into a
35:1391:94259:16:15:71:534:243:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:standard stochastic growth model (i.e., in which consumers have identical, time-invariant
35:1392:94348:15:16:71:534:228:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discount factors and idiosyncratic shocks do not exist). He allows all households to trade
35:1393:94438:16:16:71:534:212:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in a risk-free bond, but restricts one group of agents from accumulating capital.Quadrini
35:1394:94527:16:16:71:534:196:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2000)andCagetti and De Nardi(2006) study models of inequality with entrepreneurs and
35:1395:94612:16:16:72:535:180:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:workers, which can also generate skewed wealth distributions. The mechanisms have similar
35:1396:94701:16:21:72:535:164:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:flavors: agents who face higher returns end up accumulating substantial amount of wealth.
35:1397:94790:21:16:89:535:143:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The basic mechanism inGuvenen(2006) can be described as follows. Non-stockholders
35:1398:94871:16:18:72:535:127:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have a precautionary demand for wealth (bonds), but the only way they can save is if stock-
35:1399:94962:18:16:81:534:109:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:36Notice that in this paper I use-to denote the time discount factor and-was used to denote the income
35:1400:95064:16:12:72:535:93:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:growth rate. I will continue with this convention, except when I specifically refer to the Krusell-Smith model
35:1401:95174:12:0:72:319:81:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:which has come to be known as a stochastic-beta model.
36:1402:95230:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:holders are willing to borrow. In contrast, stockholders have access to capital accumulation,
36:1403:95323:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:so they could smooth consumption even if the bond market was completely shut down. Fur-
36:1404:95410:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:thermore, non-stockholders’ asset demand is even more inelastic because they are assumed
36:1405:95498:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to have a lower elasticity of intertemporal substitution (consistent with empirical evidence)
36:1406:95591:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and therefore have a strong desire for consumption smoothing. Therefore, trading bonds
36:1407:95677:16:16:72:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for consumption smoothing is more important for non-stockholders than it is for stockhold-
36:1408:95767:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ers. As a result, stockholders will only trade in the bond market if they can borrow at
36:1409:95854:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:a low interest rate. This low interest rate in turn dampens non-stockholders’ demand for
36:1410:95942:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:savings further, and they end up with little wealth in equilibrium (and stockholders end
36:1411:96030:15:16:72:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:up borrowing very little).Guvenen(2009b) shows that a calibrated version of this model
36:1412:96116:16:16:72:535:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:easily generates the extremely skewed distribution of the relative wealth of stockholders to
36:1413:96208:16:31:72:241:521:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:non-stockholders in the US data.
36:1414:96240:31:15:72:535:490:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Can we Tell them Apart?The determination of wealth inequality in the three models
36:1415:96321:15:16:72:535:475:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discussed so far can be explained using variations of a diagram used byAiyagari(1994).
36:1416:96407:16:16:71:535:459:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The left panel of figure2 shows how wealth inequality is determined in Laitner’s model and,
36:1417:96498:16:16:71:534:443:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:given their close relationship, in the Krusell-Smith model. The top solid curve originating
36:1418:96589:16:16:71:539:427:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from “-Bmin”plotthelong-runassetdemandschedulefortheimpatientagent;thebottom
36:1419:96665:16:16:71:534:411:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:curve is for the patient agent. A well-known feature of incomplete markets models is that the
36:1420:96758:16:16:71:534:395:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:asset demand schedule is very flat for values of returns that are close to the time preference
36:1421:96852:16:16:71:535:379:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rate,⌘(so-⌘1/(1 +⌘)). Thus, both types of individuals’ demand schedules asymptote
36:1422:96933:16:16:72:535:363:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to their respective time preference rates (with⌘patient<⌘impatient).37Ifthe equilibrium
36:1423:97020:16:16:72:535:347:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:return (which must be lower than⌘patientfor an equilibrium to exist) is sufficiently close
36:1424:97110:16:15:72:535:331:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to⌘patient, the high sensitivity of asset demands to interest rates will generate substantial
36:1425:97203:15:21:72:331:316:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wealth inequality between the two types of agents.
36:1426:97253:21:16:89:535:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Similarly, the right panel shows the mechanism in the limited participation model, which
36:1427:97341:16:16:72:535:279:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:has a similar flavor. For simplicity, let us focus on the case where stockholders and non-
36:1428:97431:16:16:72:535:263:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stockholders have the same preferences and face the same portfolio constraints. We have
36:1429:97518:16:16:72:538:247:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f2:⌘>RS>Rf.Again,giventhesensitivityofassetdemandtoreturnsnear⌘,evenasmall
36:1430:97589:16:16:71:534:231:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equity premium generates substantial wealth inequality.  It should be stressed, however,
36:1431:97677:16:16:71:534:215:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that a large wealth inequality is not a foregone conclusion in any of these models. If returns
36:1432:97771:16:15:71:538:199:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:were too low relative to⌘,individualswouldbeonthesteeperpartoftheirdemandcurves,
36:1433:97851:15:21:71:376:184:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which could result in smaller differences in wealth holdings.
36:1434:97912:21:16:89:535:163:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:While the mechanics described here may appear quite similar for the three models,
36:1435:97993:16:16:71:534:147:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:their substantive implications differ in crucial ways.  For example, consider the effect of
36:1436:98084:16:16:71:535:131:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:eliminating aggregate shocks from all three models.  InGuvenen(2006), there will be
36:1437:98167:16:18:71:534:115:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:no equity premium without aggregate shocks and, consequently, no wealth inequality. In
36:1438:98253:18:15:81:535:97:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:37See, for example,Aiyagari(1994) and references therein. This result also holds when asset returns are
36:1439:98356:15:0:71:268:82:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:stochastic (Chamberlain and Wilson(2000)).
37:1440:98400:0:16:72:534:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Krusell and Smith(1998), wealth inequality will increase as the patient agent holds more of
37:1441:98491:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the aggregate wealth (and would own all the wealth if there were no idiosyncratic shocks). In
37:1442:98584:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Laitner(1992), wealth inequality will remain unchanged, since it is created by idiosyncratic
37:1443:98676:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lifetime income risk. These dramatically different implications suggest that one can devise
37:1444:98767:16:30:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:methods to bring empirical evidence to bear on the relevance of these different mechanisms.
37:1445:98858:30:16:72:539:602:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Cagetti and De Nardi (2006).Cagetti and De Nardi(2006)introduceheterogeneity
37:1446:98934:16:16:72:535:586:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:across individuals in both work and entrepreneurial ability. Entrepreneurial firms operate
37:1447:99024:16:16:72:535:570:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:decreasing returns to scale production functions and higher entrepreneurial ability implies
37:1448:99115:16:16:72:539:554:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ahigheroptimalscale.Becausedebtcontractsarenotperfectlyenforceableduetolimited
37:1449:99193:16:16:72:535:538:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:commitment, business owners need to put some of their assets as collateral, a portion of
37:1450:99281:16:16:72:535:522:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which would be confiscated in case of default. Entrepreneurs with very promising projects
37:1451:99370:16:16:72:535:506:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:thus have more to lose from default, which induces them to save more for collateral, borrow
37:1452:99461:16:15:72:535:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:more against it, and reach their larger optimal scale. The model is able to generate the
37:1453:99549:15:16:72:535:475:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:extreme concentration of wealth at the top of the distribution (among households many of
37:1454:99637:16:21:72:203:459:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:whom are entrepreneurs).
37:1455:99661:21:16:89:535:438:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Although this model differs from the limited participation framework in many important
37:1456:99747:16:16:72:535:422:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ways, the differential returns to saving is a critical element for generating wealth inequality in
37:1457:99845:16:16:72:535:406:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:both models. This link could be important because many individuals in the top 1% and 5%
37:1458:99932:16:16:72:535:390:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the US wealth distribution hold significant amounts of stocks but are not entrepreneurs
37:1459:100022:16:16:72:535:374:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(hold no managerial roles), which the Cagetti/De Nardi model misses. The opposite is also
37:1460:100111:16:16:72:535:358:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:true: many very rich entrepreneurs are not stockholders (outside of their own company)
37:1461:100197:16:15:72:538:342:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which does not fit well with Guvenen’s model (seeHeaton and Lucas(2000)ontheempirical
37:1462:100282:15:16:72:535:327:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:facts about wealthy entrepreneurs and stockholders). The view that perhaps the very high
37:1463:100370:16:16:72:535:311:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wealth holdings of these individuals is driven by the higher returns that they enjoy—either
37:1464:100461:16:35:72:535:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as a stockholder or as an entrepreneur—can offer a unified theory of savings rate differences.
37:1465:100555:35:28:72:317:260:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:5.3  Wage and Earnings Inequality
37:1466:100588:28:16:72:535:232:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Because the consumption-savings decision is the cornerstone of the incomplete markets
37:1467:100673:16:16:72:535:216:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:literature, virtually every model has implications for consumption and wealth inequality.
37:1468:100762:16:16:72:535:200:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The same is not true for earnings inequality. Many models assume that labor supply is
37:1469:100847:16:16:72:535:184:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:inelastic and the stochastic process for wages is exogenous, making the implications for wage
37:1470:100940:16:16:72:535:168:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and earnings inequality to be mechanical reflections of the assumptions of the model. Even
37:1471:101030:16:15:72:535:152:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:if labor supply is assumed to be endogenous, many properties of the earnings distribution
37:1472:101119:15:16:72:535:137:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(exceptions noted below) mimic those of the wage distribution.  For things to get more
37:1473:101205:16:21:72:407:121:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:interesting, it is the latter which needs to be endogenized as well.
37:1474:101273:21:16:89:535:100:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In this section, I first review the empirical facts regarding wage inequality—both over
37:1475:101360:16:0:72:535:84:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the life cycle and over time. These facts are useful to know for practitioners since they are
38:1476:101455:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:commonly used as exogenous inputs into incomplete markets models. Unless specifically
38:1477:101540:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mentioned, all the facts discussed here pertain to male workers, because the bulk of the
38:1478:101628:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:existing work is available consistently for this group.38Second, I discuss models that attempt
38:1479:101722:16:30:71:394:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to endogenize wages and explain the reported facts and trends.
38:1480:101784:30:29:71:283:618:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f20:5.3.1  Inequality Over the Lifecycle
38:1481:101820:29:16:71:534:589:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The main facts about the evolution of (within-cohort) earnings inequality over the lifecycle
38:1482:101912:16:16:71:535:573:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have first been documented byDeaton and Paxson(1994) and shown in the left panel of
38:1483:101995:16:16:71:535:557:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:figure1. The same exercise has been repeated by numerous authors using different datasets
38:1484:102084:16:16:71:534:541:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:or time periods (among others,Storesletten et al.(2004b), Guvenen(2009a),Heathcote et
38:1485:102169:16:16:71:535:525:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:al.  (2010), andKaplan(2010)). While the magnitudes differ somewhat, the basic fact that
38:1486:102257:16:20:72:503:509:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wage and earnings inequality rise substantially over the life cycle is well-established.
38:1487:102345:20:16:89:535:489:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:One view is that this fact does not require an elaborate explanation, because wages
38:1488:102428:16:16:72:535:473:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:follow a very persistent, perhaps permanent, stochastic process as implied by the RIP
38:1489:102513:16:16:72:535:457:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model. Thus, the rising lifecycle inequality is simply a reflection of the accumulation of
38:1490:102603:16:16:72:535:441:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:such shocks, which drives up the variance of log wages in a linear fashion (in the case of
38:1491:102693:16:16:72:535:425:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:permanent shocks). I will continue to refer to this view as the RIP model because of its
38:1492:102781:16:21:72:244:409:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:emphasis on persistent “shocks.”39
38:1493:102815:21:16:89:535:388:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:An alternative perspective, which has received attention more recently, emphasizes sys-
38:1494:102902:16:15:71:534:372:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tematic factors—heterogeneity as opposed to random shocks. This view is essentially in
38:1495:102988:15:16:71:534:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the same spirit as the HIP model of the previous section. But it goes one step further by
38:1496:103077:16:16:71:535:341:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f2:endogenizingthe wage distribution based on the human capital framework ofBecker(1964)
38:1497:103162:16:16:71:539:325:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and   Ben-Porath(1967)amongothers. Inaninfluentialpaper,Huggett et al.(2006)have
38:1498:103242:16:16:71:538:309:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:studied the distributional implications of the standardBen-Porath(1967)modelbyasking
38:1499:103326:16:16:72:535:293:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the types of heterogeneity that one needs to introduce to generate patterns consistent with
38:1500:103417:16:16:72:535:277:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the US data. They find that too much heterogeneity in initial human capital levels results
38:1501:103507:16:16:72:535:261:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in the counterfactual implication that wage inequalityshould fallover the lifecycle.  In
38:1502:103595:16:16:72:535:245:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:contrast, heterogeneity in the learning ability generates rise in wage inequality consistent
38:1503:103687:16:15:72:535:229:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with the data. A key implication of this finding is that the rise in wage inequality can be
38:1504:103778:15:16:72:535:214:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:generated without appealing to idiosyncratic shocks of any kind. Instead, it is the system-
38:1505:103869:16:16:72:535:198:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:atic fanning out of wage profiles, resulting from different investment rates, that generates
38:1506:103961:16:16:72:535:182:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:rising inequality over the life cycle.Guvenen et al.(2009)andHuggett et al.(forthcoming)
38:1507:104049:16:16:71:534:166:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:introduce idiosyncratic shocks into the Ben-Porath framework. Both papers find that het-
38:1508:104137:16:18:71:534:150:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:erogeneous growth rates continue to play the dominant role for the rise in wage inequality.
38:1509:104228:18:15:81:535:132:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:38Some of the empirical trends discussed below also apply to women, while others do not. SeeAutor et
38:1510:104328:15:9:71:465:117:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:al. (2008)foracomparativelookatwagetrendsformalesandfemalesduringtheperiod.
38:1511:104403:9:15:81:534:108:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:39Of course, one can write deeper economic models which generates the the observation that wages
38:1512:104499:15:12:71:539:93:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:follow a random walk process, such as the learning model ofJovanovic(1979)inasearchandmatching
38:1513:104593:12:0:71:533:81:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:environment, or the optimal contracts in the limited commitment model ofHarris and Holmstrom(1982).
39:1514:104694:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The Ben-Porath formulation is also central for wage determination inHeckman et al.(1998)
39:1515:104782:16:31:72:193:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and   Kitao et al.(2008).
39:1516:104807:31:28:72:285:649:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f20:5.3.2  Inequality Trends Over Time
39:1517:104841:28:16:72:540:621:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Awell-documentedempiricaltrendsincethe1970sistheriseinwageinequalityamong
39:1518:104914:16:16:72:535:605:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:male workers in the United States. This trend has been especially prominent above the
39:1519:104999:16:16:72:535:589:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:median of the wage distribution: for example, the log wage differential between the 90th
39:1520:105087:16:16:72:535:573:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and the 50th percentiles has been expanding in a secular fashion for the past four decades.
39:1521:105178:16:16:72:535:557:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The changes at the bottom have been more episodic, with the log 50-10 wage differential
39:1522:105265:16:16:72:535:541:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:strongly expanding until late 1980s and then closing subsequently (seeAutor et al.(2008)
39:1523:105353:16:16:72:539:525:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for a detailed review of the evidence).Acemoglu(2002)containsanextensivesummary
39:1524:105432:16:15:71:534:509:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of several related wage trends as well as a review of proposed explanations. Here I only
39:1525:105520:15:16:71:534:494:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discuss the subset of papers that are more closely relevant for the incomplete markets macro
39:1526:105612:16:31:71:122:478:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:literature.
39:1527:105623:31:16:71:535:447:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Larger Shocks or Increasing Heterogeneity?Economists’ interpretations of the rise
39:1528:105704:16:15:71:534:431:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in wage inequality over the life cycle and over time are intimately related. The RIP view that
39:1529:105798:15:16:71:534:416:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:was motivated by analyses of life-cycle wages was dominant in the 1980s and 1990s, so it was
39:1530:105890:16:16:71:539:400:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:natural for economists to interpret the rise in wage inequalityover time,throughthesame
39:1531:105977:16:16:71:535:384:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lens. Starting withGottschalk and Moffitt(1994)andMoffitt and Gottschalk(1995), this
39:1532:106061:16:16:71:534:368:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:trend has been broadly interpreted as reflecting a rise in the variances of idiosyncratic shocks,
39:1533:106158:16:16:71:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:either permanent or transitory (Meghir and Pistaferri(2004),Heathcote et al.(2008), etc.).
39:1534:106248:16:16:71:534:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This approach remains the dominant way to calibrate economic models that investigate
39:1535:106332:16:21:71:349:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:changes in economic outcomes from the 1970s to date.
39:1536:106384:21:16:89:535:299:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:However, some recent papers have documented new evidence that seems hard to reconcile
39:1537:106469:16:15:71:534:283:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with the RIP view. The first group of papers revisit the econometric analyses of wage and
39:1538:106558:15:16:71:539:268:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:earnings data. Among these,Sabelhaus and Song(2009,2010)haveusedpaneldatafrom
39:1539:106635:16:16:71:534:252:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Social Security records covering millions of American workers, in contrast to the long list of
39:1540:106729:16:16:71:535:236:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:previous studies that use survey data (e.g., the PSID).40While this dataset has the potential
39:1541:106822:16:16:71:534:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:drawback of under-reporting (because it is based on income reported to the IRS), it has
39:1542:106909:16:16:71:534:204:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:three important advantages: (i) a much larger sample size (on the order of 50+ million
39:1543:106995:16:16:71:534:188:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:observations, compared to at most 50,000 in the PSID), (ii) no survey response error, and
39:1544:107084:16:16:71:534:172:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(iii) no attrition. Sabelhaus and Song found that the volatility of annual earnings growth
39:1545:107174:16:16:71:535:156:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:increased during the 1970s, but that itdeclinedmonotonically during the 1980s and 1990s.
39:1546:107262:16:15:71:535:140:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Furthermore, applying the standard permanent-transitory decomposition as inMoffitt and
39:1547:107348:15:19:71:538:125:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Gottschalk(1995)andMeghir and Pistaferri(2004)revealsthatpermanentshockvariances
39:1548:107428:19:16:81:534:106:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:40These include, among others,Meghir and Pistaferri(2004),Dynan et al.(2007),Heathcote et al.(2008),
39:1549:107528:16:0:71:190:90:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:and   Solon and Shin(2011).
40:1550:107557:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:were stable and transitory shocks becamesmallerfrom 1980 into the 2000s. A separate
40:1551:107640:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:study conducted by theCongressional Budget Office(2008), also using wage earnings from
40:1552:107726:16:16:72:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Social Security records from 1980 to 2003, reached the same conclusion.41Finally,Kopczuk
40:1553:107814:16:16:71:539:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(2010)document(alsousingSocialSecuritydata)thatbothlong-runandshort-run
40:1554:107891:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mobility have stayed remarkably stable from 1960s into the 2000s. But this finding seems
40:1555:107979:16:16:71:539:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:difficult to reconcile withMoffitt and Gottschalk(1995)andthesubsequentliteraturethat
40:1556:108064:16:16:71:534:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:found permanent and transitory shock variances to have risen in different sub-periods from
40:1557:108154:16:16:71:534:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:1970 to 2000s. If true, the latter would result in fluctuations in mobility patterns over these
40:1558:108249:16:19:71:437:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sub-periods, which is not borne out inKopczuk et al.(2010)’s analysis.
40:1559:108319:19:16:89:534:549:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Another piece of evidence from income data is offered byHaider(2001), who estimated a
40:1560:108404:16:16:71:538:533:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stochastic process for wages similar to the one inMoffitt and Gottschalk(1995)andothers,
40:1561:108492:16:16:71:535:517:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:but with one key difference. He allowed for individual-specific wage growth rates (HIP)
40:1562:108579:16:16:71:535:501:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f2:andhe also allowed for the dispersion of growth rates to vary over time. The stochastic
40:1563:108666:16:16:71:534:485:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:component is specified as an ARMA(1,1). With this more flexible specification, he found
40:1564:108753:16:15:71:534:469:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:no evidence of a rise in the variance of income shocks after 1970s, but instead found a large
40:1565:108846:15:20:71:371:454:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:increase in the dispersion of systematic wage growth rates.
40:1566:108905:20:16:89:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:A second strand of the literature have studied the trends in labor market flows in the
40:1567:108991:16:16:71:534:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:United States. These studies do not find any evidence of rising job instability or churning,
40:1568:109083:16:16:71:534:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which one might expect to see in conjunction with larger idiosyncratic shocks. In contrast,
40:1569:109174:16:16:71:534:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:these studies document an across-the-board moderation in labor market flows. For example,
40:1570:109263:16:15:71:538:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Gottschalk and Moffitt(1999)focusonmaleworkersbetweenages20and62andconclude
40:1571:109338:15:26:71:195:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:their analysis as follows:
40:1572:109364:26:16:101:506:329:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:[W]e believe that a consistent picture is emerging on changes in job stability
40:1573:109442:16:16:101:506:313:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and job security in the 1980s and 1990s. Job instability does not seem to have
40:1574:109520:16:16:101:506:297:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:increased, and the consequences of separating from an employer do not seem to
40:1575:109597:16:26:101:186:281:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:have worsened.42
40:1576:109613:26:16:72:538:255:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Shimer(2005,2007)andDavis et al.(2010)extendthisanalysistocoverthe2000sandusea
40:1577:109691:16:15:72:535:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:variety of datasets to reach the same conclusion. Further, both papers show that expanding
40:1578:109781:15:16:72:534:224:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the sample of individuals to include women and younger workers shows adecliningtrend
40:1579:109865:16:17:72:327:208:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in labor market flows andincreasein job security.
40:1580:109914:17:15:81:534:191:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:41Sabelhaus-Song attribute the reason why some earlier studies found rising variances of wage shocks
40:1581:110014:15:12:71:534:176:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:(e.g.,Moffitt and Gottschalk(2008)) to the inclusion of individuals with self-employment income and those
40:1582:110119:12:12:71:534:164:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:who earn less than the Social Security minimum. Even though there are few of these households, they show
40:1583:110223:12:12:71:539:152:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:that they make a big difference in the computed statistics. Similarly,Solon and Shin(2011,p. 978-980)
40:1584:110324:12:12:71:534:140:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:use PSID data and also do not find a trend in the volatility of wage earnings changes during the 1980s and
40:1585:110430:12:12:71:538:128:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:1990s. They argue that the increasing volatility found in earlier studies, such asDynan et al.(2007)seems
40:1586:110535:12:12:71:534:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:to be coming from the inclusion of some auxiliary types of income (from business, farming, etc) whose
40:1587:110636:12:9:71:332:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:treatment has been inconsistent in the PSID over the years.
40:1588:110695:9:15:81:534:95:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:42They also say, “Almost all studies based on the various Current Population Surveys (CPS) supplements
40:1589:110797:15:0:71:403:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:...show little change in the overall separation rates through the early 1990s.”
41:1590:110878:0:16:72:534:696:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Taking Stock.To summarize, the seeming consensus of the 1990s—that rising wage
41:1591:110956:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:inequality was driven by an increase in idiosyncratic shock variances—is being challenged
41:1592:111045:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by a variety of new evidence, some of which from data sets many orders of magnitude
41:1593:111128:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:larger than the surveys used in previous analyses.  In addition, the evidence from labor
41:1594:111216:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:market flows described above—while perhaps more indirect—raises questions about the
41:1595:111299:16:16:72:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sources of larger idiosyncratic shocks in a period where labor market transitions seem to
41:1596:111388:16:16:72:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have moderated. Although, it would be premature to conclude that the alternative view
41:1597:111473:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is the correct one—more evidence is needed to reach a definitive conclusion. Having said
41:1598:111561:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that, if this alternative viewistrue, and income shock variances have not increased, this
41:1599:111650:15:16:72:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:new “fact” would require economists to rethink a variety of explanations put forward for
41:1600:111738:16:40:72:479:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:various trends, which took as given a rise in shock variances during this period.
41:1601:111819:40:33:72:425:497:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:6HeterogeneitywithAggregateShocks
41:1602:111852:33:15:72:538:464:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Krusell and Smith(1998)addedtwoelementstothebasicAiyagariframework.Firstthey
41:1603:111928:15:16:72:535:449:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:introduced aggregate technology shocks. Second, they assumed that the cumulative discount
41:1604:112017:16:16:72:534:433:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:factor at timet(which was assumed to be-tbefore), now follows the stochastic process
41:1605:112101:16:16:71:535:417:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f2:-t= ̃--t-1,where ̃-is a finite-state Markov chain. The stochastic evolution of the discount
41:1606:112192:16:16:71:534:401:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:factors within a dynasty captures some elements of an explicit overlapping-generations
41:1607:112278:16:16:71:534:385:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:structure with altruism and less than perfect correlation in genes between parents and
41:1608:112364:16:16:71:535:369:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:children, as inLaitner(1992).  With this interpretation in mind, the evolution of ̃-is

41:1611:112621:16:20:71:498:321:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model where consumers are allowed to hold a risk-free bond in addition to capital.)

41:1618:113173:34:16:89:535:174:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Finally, the entire wealth distribution, which I denote with-is a state variable for this

41:1622:113348:34:28:72:280:124:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:6.1  Krusell-Smith Algorithm
41:1623:113376:28:16:72:544:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Akeyequilibriumobjectinthisclassofmodelsisthelawofmotion,H.Inprinciple,
41:1624:113447:16:0:72:535:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:computing this object is a formidable task since the distribution of wealth is infinite-
42:1625:113537:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dimensional.Krusell and Smith(1997,1998) show, however, that this class of models,
42:1626:113619:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:when reasonably parameterized, exhibits “approximate aggregation”: loosely speaking, to
42:1627:113706:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:predict future prices consumers need to forecast only a small set of statistics of the wealth
42:1628:113799:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:distribution rather than the entire distribution itself. This result makes it possible to use
42:1629:113892:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:numerical methods to analyze this class of models. Another key feature of the Krusell-Smith
42:1630:113983:16:16:72:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:algorithm is that it solves the model by simulating it. Specifically, the basic version of the
42:1631:114077:16:31:72:211:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:algorithm works as follows:
42:1632:114104:31:15:86:535:569:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:1. Approximate-with a finite number (I)ofmoments.(Hreduces to a function map-
42:1633:114181:15:29:101:515:554:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ping theImoments today into theImoments tomorrow depending onztoday.)
42:1634:114250:29:29:115:448:525:143:g_d0_f52:64:g_d0_f4:•We will start by selecting one moment—the mean—soI=1.43
42:1635:114306:29:16:86:535:496:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:2. Select a family of functions forH. I will choose a log-linear function following Krusell
42:1636:114397:16:29:101:158:480:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and Smith.
42:1637:114407:29:8:163:262:451:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:V(k,✏;-,z)=max
42:1638:114421:8:0:242:255:443:64:g_d0_f15:36:g_d0_f29:c,k0
42:1639:114425:0:13:261:267:464:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:h
42:1640:114426:13:0:267:343:451:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f13:U(c)+-E[V(k
42:1641:114437:0:8:344:346:459:36:g_d0_f29:36:g_d0_f29:0
42:1642:114438:8:0:347:359:451:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f19:,✏
42:1643:114440:0:8:357:359:459:36:g_d0_f29:36:g_d0_f29:0
42:1644:114441:8:0:360:374:451:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f31:;-
42:1645:114443:0:8:373:375:459:36:g_d0_f29:36:g_d0_f29:0

42:1647:114446:0:8:387:389:459:36:g_d0_f29:36:g_d0_f29:0

42:1649:114453:0:39:419:425:464:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:i
42:1650:114454:39:18:193:472:425:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:c+k0=w(K, L, z)⇥l⇥✏+r(K, L, z)⇥k,k0-0
42:1651:114491:18:19:191:376:407:143:g_d0_f14:64:g_d0_f15:logK0=a0+a1logKforz=zb

42:1653:114535:34:16:86:535:354:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:3. Make an (educated) initial guess about(a0,a1,b0,b1))yields initial guess forH0.
42:1654:114617:16:26:101:269:338:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Make also an initial guess for-0.
42:1655:114650:26:16:86:535:312:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:4. Solve the consumer’s dynamic program. Using only the resulting decision rules, sim-
42:1656:114736:16:28:101:281:296:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ulate{kn,t}N,Tn=1,t=1for(N, T)large.
42:1657:114772:28:0:86:304:268:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f15:5. UpdateHby estimating (whereeK=1N
42:1658:114807:0:12:307:327:277:143:g_d0_f18:64:g_d0_f15:PN

42:1660:114816:26:20:225:410:239:143:g_d0_f14:64:g_d0_f15:logeK0=a0+a1logeKforz=zb
