42:1662:114864:34:16:86:535:185:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:6. Iterate on 4-5, until theR2of this regression is “sufficiently high” and the forecast
42:1663:114952:16:29:101:196:169:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:variance is “small.”
42:1664:114972:29:18:115:459:140:143:g_d0_f52:143:g_d0_f6:•If accuracy remains insufficient, go back to step 1 and increaseI.
42:1665:115039:18:16:81:534:122:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:43When we add more moments, we do not have to proceed as mean, variance, skewness, and so on. We
42:1666:115135:16:12:71:534:106:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:can include, say, the wealth holdings of the top 10 percent of population, mean- to-median wealth ratio,
42:1667:115239:12:0:71:86:94:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:etc.
43:1668:115245:0:27:72:156:696:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:6.2  Details
43:1669:115257:27:16:72:535:669:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Educated Initial Guess.As with many numerical methods, a good initial guess is criti-
43:1670:115342:16:16:72:535:653:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cal. More often than not, the success or failure of a given algorithm will depend on the initial
43:1671:115438:16:16:72:535:637:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:guess. One idea (used by Krusell and Smith) is to first solve a standard representative-agent
43:1672:115531:16:16:72:535:621:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f14:RBC model with the same parameterization. Then estimate the coefficients(a0,a1,b0,b1)
43:1673:115616:16:16:72:534:605:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:using capital series simulated from this model to obtain an initial guess for step 1 above.44
43:1674:115709:16:16:72:535:589:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:More generally, a good initial guess can often be obtained by solving a simplified version
43:1675:115799:16:16:72:535:573:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the full model. Sometimes this simplification involves ignoring certain constraints, some-
43:1676:115892:16:28:72:328:557:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:times by shutting down certain shocks, and so on.
43:1677:115941:28:16:72:534:529:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Discretizing an AR(1) Process.Oftentimes, the exogenous driving force in incomplete
43:1678:116024:16:16:72:535:513:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:markets models is assumed to be generated by an AR(1) process, which is discretized and
43:1679:116111:16:15:72:535:497:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:converted into a Markov chain.  One popular method for discretization is described in
43:1680:116196:15:16:72:539:482:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Aiyagari(1993)andhasbeenusedextensivelyintheliterature. However,analternative
43:1681:116273:16:16:72:535:466:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:method due toRouwenhorst(1995) (and which received far less attention until recently) is
43:1682:116361:16:16:72:535:450:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:far superior in the quality of the approximation that it provides, especially when the process
43:1683:116455:16:16:72:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is very persistent, which is often the case. Moreover, it is very easy to implement.Kopecky
43:1684:116546:16:16:72:537:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and Suen(2010)andLkhagvasuren and Galindev(2010)providecomprehensivecomparisons
43:1685:116625:16:16:72:535:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of different discretization methods, which reveal the general superiority ofRouwenhorst
43:1686:116712:16:16:72:535:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1995)’s method.  They also show how this method can be extended to discretize more
43:1687:116795:16:28:72:162:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:general processes.
43:1688:116813:28:16:72:535:342:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Non-Trivial Equilibrium Pricing Function.One simplifying feature ofKrusell and
43:1689:116891:16:15:71:539:326:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Smith(1998)isthatequilibriumprices(wagesandinterestrates)aredeterminedtrivially
43:1690:116970:15:16:71:535:311:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by the marginal product conditions (12). Thus they depend only on the aggregate capital
43:1691:117057:16:16:71:534:295:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stock and not on its distribution. Some models do not have this structure—instead pricing
43:1692:117146:16:16:71:534:279:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:functions must be determined by equilibrium conditions—such as market-clearing or zero-
43:1693:117233:16:16:71:534:263:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:profit conditions—that explicitly depend on the wealth distribution.  This would be the
43:1694:117320:16:16:71:534:247:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:case, for example, if a household bond is traded in the economy. Its price must be solved
43:1695:117409:16:16:71:534:231:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for using market clearing condition, which is a challenging task.  Moreover, if there is
43:1696:117497:16:16:71:534:215:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:an additional asset, such as a stock, two prices must be determined simultaneously, and
43:1697:117584:16:16:71:534:199:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this must be done in such a way that avoids providing arbitrage opportunities—along the
43:1698:117671:16:15:71:534:183:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:iterations of the solution algorithm. Otherwise, individuals’ portfolio choices will go haywire
43:1699:117766:15:16:71:534:168:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(in an attempt to take advantage of perceived arbitrage), wreaking havoc with the solution
43:1700:117856:16:16:71:539:152:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:algorithm.Krusell and Smith(1997)solvedsuchamodelandproposedanalgorithmto
43:1701:117929:16:17:71:443:136:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tackle these issues. I refer the interested reader to that paper for details.
43:1702:118006:17:15:81:538:119:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:44Can’t we updateHwithout simulating? Yes we can.den Haan and Rendahl(2009)proposeamethod
43:1703:118095:15:12:72:535:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:where they use the policy functions for capital holdings and integrate them over distribution⇤(k,✏)of
43:1704:118196:12:0:71:367:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f23:households across capital and employment status:K0=Hj(K,z)=
43:1705:118255:0:8:367:372:100:99:g_d0_f18:99:g_d0_f18:R
43:1706:118256:8:12:376:535:92:99:g_d0_f21:99:g_d0_f8:k0j(k,✏;-,z)d⇤(k,✏). This works well
43:1707:118292:12:0:71:498:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:when the decision rules are parameterized in a particular way. Seeden Haan and Rendahl(2009).
44:1708:118387:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Checking for Accuracy of Solution.Many studies with aggregate fluctuations and
44:1709:118465:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneity use two simple criteria to asses the accuracy of the law of motion in their
44:1710:118554:16:29:72:446:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:limited information approximation. If agents are using the law of motion
44:1711:118626:29:29:220:535:635:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f2:logK0=↵1+↵2z+↵3logK+u(13)
44:1712:118651:29:16:71:535:606:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aperfectlysolvedmodelshouldfindu=0. Thus, practitioners will continue to solve the
44:1713:118733:16:16:72:535:590:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model until either theR2of this regression is larger than some minimum or-ufalls below
44:1714:118819:16:21:72:316:574:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:some threshold (step 6 in the algorithm above).
44:1715:118866:21:16:89:535:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:However, one shouldnotrely solely onR2and-u. There are at least three reasons for
44:1716:118947:16:16:72:535:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this (den Haan(2010)). First, both measures average over all periods of the simulation.
44:1717:119034:16:16:72:535:521:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Thus, infrequent but large deviations from the forecast rule can be hidden in the average.
44:1718:119124:16:15:72:535:505:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:These errors may be very important to agents and their decision rule. For example, the
44:1719:119210:15:16:72:535:490:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:threat of a very large recession may increase buffer stock saving, but the approximation
44:1720:119298:16:16:72:535:474:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:may understate the movement of capital in such a case. Second, and more importantly,
44:1721:119382:16:16:72:535:458:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:these statistics only measure one-step ahead forecasts. The regression only considers the
44:1722:119471:16:16:72:535:442:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dynamics from one period to the next, so errors are only the deviations between the actual
44:1723:119561:16:16:72:535:426:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:next-period capital and the expected amount in the next period. This misses potentially
44:1724:119648:16:16:72:535:410:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:large deviations between thelong-termforecast for capital and its actual level. Aware of
44:1725:119736:16:16:72:535:394:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this possibility,Krusell and Smith(1998)alsocheckedtheR2for forecasting prices 25 years
44:1726:119823:16:16:71:534:378:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ahead (100 model periods) and found it to be extremely high as well! (They also check the
44:1727:119912:16:16:71:535:362:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:maximum error in long-term forecasts, which was very small.) Third,R2is scaled by the
44:1728:119997:16:29:71:376:346:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:LHS of the regression. An alternative is to check theR2of:
44:1729:120055:29:34:194:411:317:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f13:logK0-logK=↵1+↵2z+(↵3-1) logK
44:1730:120084:34:15:89:539:283:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:As a particularly dramatic demonstration,den Haan(2010)usesasavingsdecisionrule
44:1731:120163:15:16:71:535:268:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that solves theKrusell and Smith(1998)model,simulatesitforTperiods and estimates a
44:1732:120245:16:0:71:495:252:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f17:law of motion in the form of equation (13). He then manipulates↵1,↵3such thatT-1
44:1733:120325:0:9:498:511:261:143:g_d0_f18:143:g_d0_f18:P
44:1734:120326:9:16:512:535:252:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:ut=
44:1735:120329:16:16:72:535:236:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f2:0but theR2falls from0.9999to0.999and then0.99. This has economically meaningful
44:1736:120408:16:16:72:535:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:consequences: the time series standard deviation of the capital stock simulated from the
44:1737:120496:16:21:72:481:204:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:perturbed version of equation (13)fallsto70%and then46%of the true figure.
44:1738:120570:21:16:89:535:183:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Finally,den Haan(2010) proposes a useful test that begins with the approximated law
44:1739:120653:16:16:71:120:167:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of motion
44:1740:120662:16:23:220:535:151:143:g_d0_f14:143:g_d0_f2:logK0=ˆ↵1+ˆ↵2z+ˆ↵3logK+u(14)
44:1741:120690:23:16:71:534:128:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to generate a sequence of realizations of{eKt+1}Tt=0and then compare these to the sequence
44:1742:120780:16:15:72:534:112:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f17:generated by aggregating from decision rules, the true law of motion. Because{eKt+1}Tt=0
44:1743:120868:15:16:72:539:97:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is obtained by repeatedly applying Equation (14)startingfromeK0,errorscanaccumulate.
44:1744:120952:16:0:71:534:81:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This is important because in the true model, today’s choices depend upon expectations
45:1745:121039:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:about the future state, which in turn depends upon the future’s future expectations and
45:1746:121126:16:16:72:540:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:so errors cascade. To systematically compareeKttoKt,denHaanproposesan“essential
45:1747:121205:16:16:71:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:accuracy plot.” For a sequence of shocks (notthose originally used when estimating↵’s to
45:1748:121293:16:16:71:540:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:solve the model) generate a sequence ofeKtandKt.Onecanthencomparemomentsofthe
45:1749:121370:16:16:71:534:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:two simulated sequences. The “main focus” of the accuracy test are the errors calculated
45:1750:121458:16:29:71:445:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:byeut=|logeKt-logKt|, whose maximum should be made close to zero.
45:1751:121523:29:16:71:535:587:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Prices Are More Sensitive Than Quantities.The accuracy of the numerical solution
45:1752:121603:16:16:71:535:571:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:becomes an even more critical issue if the main focus of analysis is (asset) prices rather
45:1753:121693:16:16:71:534:555:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:than quantities. This is because prices are much more sensitive to approximation errors
45:1754:121780:16:15:71:534:539:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(see, e.g.,Christiano and Fisher(2000), andJudd and Guu(2001)). The results inChris-
45:1755:121864:15:16:71:535:524:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tiano and Fisher(2000) are especially striking. These authors compare a variety of different
45:1756:121956:16:16:71:534:508:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:implementations of the “parameterized expectations” method and report the approximation
45:1757:122043:16:16:71:534:492:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:errors resulting from each. For the standard deviation of output, consumption, and invest-
45:1758:122133:16:16:71:534:476:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ment (i.e., “quantities”) the approximation errors range from less than 0.1% of the true value
45:1759:122227:16:16:71:534:460:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to 1-2% in some cases. For the stock and bond return and the equity premium, the errors
45:1760:122314:16:16:71:534:444:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:regularly exceed 50% and are greater than 100% in several cases. The bottom-line is that
45:1761:122402:16:29:71:328:428:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the computation of asset prices requireextracare.
45:1762:122451:29:16:71:533:399:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Pros and Cons.An important feature of the Krusell-Smith method is that it is a “local”
45:1763:122537:16:16:71:534:383:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:solution around the stationary recursive equilibrium. In other words, this method relies
45:1764:122625:16:16:71:534:367:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on simulating a very long time series of data (e.g., capital series) and making sure that
45:1765:122714:16:15:71:534:351:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:after this path has converged to the ergodic set, the predictions of agents are accurate for
45:1766:122806:15:16:71:534:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:behavior inside that set. This has some advantages and some disadvantages. On advantage
45:1767:122893:16:16:71:535:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is the efficiency gain compared to solving a full recursive equilibrium, which enforces the
45:1768:122984:16:16:71:534:304:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:equilibrium conditions at every point of a somewhat arbitrary grid, regardless of whether
45:1769:123073:16:20:71:400:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:or not a given state is ever visited in the stationary equilibrium.
45:1770:123140:20:16:89:535:268:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:One disadvantage is that if you take a larger deviation—say by settingK0to a value
45:1771:123222:16:16:71:534:252:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:well below the steady state value—your “equilibrium functions” are likely to be inaccurate,
45:1772:123313:16:16:71:534:236:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and the behavior of the solution may differ significantly from the true solution. Why should
45:1773:123405:16:16:71:534:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:we care about this? Suppose you solve your model then want to study a policy experiment
45:1774:123492:16:16:71:534:204:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:where you eliminate taxes on savings. You would need to write a separate program from
45:1775:123577:16:15:71:534:188:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the “transition” between the two stationary equilibria.  Instead, if you solve for the full
45:1776:123668:15:16:71:534:173:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:recursive equilibrium over a grid that contains both the initial and final steady states, you
45:1777:123761:16:16:71:534:157:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:would not need to do this. However, solving for the full equilibrium is often much harder
45:1778:123850:16:29:71:243:141:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and, therefore, is often “over-kill.”
45:1779:123887:29:16:71:534:112:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:An Alternative to Krusell-Smith: Tracking History of Shocks.Some models have
45:1780:123963:16:16:71:534:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:few exogenous state variables, but a large number of endogenous states. In such cases, using
45:1781:124055:16:0:71:538:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aformulationthatkeepstrackofallthesestatevariablescanmakethenumericalsolution
46:1782:124134:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:extremely costly or even infeasible. An alternative method begins with the straightforward
46:1783:124224:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:observation that all current endogenous state variables are nothing more than functions of
46:1784:124314:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the infinite history of exogenous shocks. So, one could replace these endogenous states with
46:1785:124406:16:16:72:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the infinite history of exogenous states. Moreover, many models turn out to have “limited
46:1786:124495:16:16:72:535:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:memory” in the sense that only the recent history of shocks matters in a quantitatively
46:1787:124582:16:16:72:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:significant way, allowing us to only track a truncated history of exogenous states. The first
46:1788:124675:16:16:72:534:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:implementation of this idea I have been able to find is inVeracierto(1997), who studied a
46:1789:124764:16:16:72:535:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:model with plant-level investment irreversibilities, which give rise to S-s type policies. He
46:1790:124857:16:15:72:535:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:showed that it is more practical to track a short history of the S-s thresholds instead of the
46:1791:124951:15:21:72:288:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:current-period endogenous state variables.
46:1792:124993:21:16:89:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:As another example, consider an equilibrium model of the housing market where the
46:1793:125074:16:16:72:535:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:only exogenous state is the interest rate, which evolves as a Markov process. Depending
46:1794:125161:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on the precise model structure, the individual endogenous state variables can include the
46:1795:125250:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mortgage debt outstanding, the time-to-maturity of the mortgage contract, etc., and the
46:1796:125337:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate endogenous state can include the entire distribution of agents over the individual
46:1797:125429:16:16:72:538:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:states. This is potentially an enormously large state space!Arslan(2011)successfullysolves
46:1798:125519:16:15:72:535:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:a model of this sort with realistic fixed-rate mortgage contracts, a lifecycle structure, and
46:1799:125612:15:16:72:535:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stochastic interest rates, using 4 lags of interest rates. Other recent examples that employ
46:1800:125704:16:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this basic approach includeLustig and Chien(2010) who solve an asset pricing model with
46:1801:125791:16:16:72:535:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate and idiosyncratic risk in which agents are subject to collateral constraints arising
46:1802:125885:16:16:72:535:373:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from limited commitment, andLorenzoni(2009) who solves a business cycle model with
46:1803:125967:16:16:71:534:357:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:shocks to individuals’ expectations. In all these cases, tracking a truncated history turns
46:1804:126058:16:16:71:534:341:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:out to provide computational advantages over choosing endogenous state variables that
46:1805:126143:16:16:71:534:325:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:evolve in a Markovian fashion. One advantage of this approach is that it is often less costly
46:1806:126236:16:16:71:534:309:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to add an extra endogenous state variable relative to the standard approach, because the
46:1807:126324:16:15:71:535:293:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:same number of lags may still be sufficient. One drawback is that if the Markov process
46:1808:126411:15:40:72:496:278:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:has many states or the model has long memory, the method may not work as well.
46:1809:126489:40:33:72:511:238:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:7  When Does Heterogeneity Matter for Aggregates?
46:1810:126538:33:16:72:540:205:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:As noted earlier,Krusell and Smith(1998)reportthatthetimeseriesbehaviorofthe
46:1811:126614:16:16:72:535:189:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregated incomplete markets model, by and large, looks very similar to the corresponding
46:1812:126704:16:16:72:535:173:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:representative-agent model. A similar result was reported inRios-Rull(1996). However,
46:1813:126789:16:16:72:535:157:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:it is important to interpret these findings correctly and to not overgeneralize them. For
46:1814:126878:16:16:72:539:141:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:example, even if a model aggregatesexactly,modelingheterogeneitycanbeveryimportant
46:1815:126960:16:15:72:535:125:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for aggregate problems. This is because the problem solved by the representative agent
46:1816:127046:15:16:72:535:110:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:can look dramatically different from the problem solved by individuals (for example, have
46:1817:127135:16:0:72:535:94:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:very different preferences). Here, I discuss some important problems in macroeconomics
47:1818:127223:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:where introducing heterogeneity yields conclusions quite different from a representative-
47:1819:127312:16:34:72:138:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:agent model.
47:1820:127324:34:28:72:297:646:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:7.1  The Curse of Long Horizon
47:1821:127354:28:16:72:535:618:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:It is useful to start by discussing why incomplete markets do not matter in many models.
47:1822:127442:16:16:72:535:602:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Loosely speaking, this outcome follows from the fact that a long horizon makes individuals’
47:1823:127533:16:16:72:535:586:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:savings function approximately linear in wealth (i.e., constant MPC out of wealth). As we
47:1824:127622:16:16:72:535:570:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:saw in Section 2, the exact linearity of savings rule delivered exact demand aggregation
47:1825:127710:16:15:72:535:554:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in bothGorman(1961)andRubinstein(1974)’s theorems.  As it turns out, even with
47:1826:127788:15:16:72:535:539:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic shocks, this near-linearity holds for wealth levels that are not immediately near
47:1827:127883:16:16:72:535:523:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:borrowing constraints. Thus, even though markets are incomplete, redistributing wealth
47:1828:127969:16:21:72:482:507:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:would matter little, and we have something that looks like demand aggregation!
47:1829:128047:21:16:89:535:486:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Is there a way to get around this result? It is instructive to look at a concrete example.
47:1830:128137:16:15:72:539:470:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Mankiw(1986)wasoneofthefirstpapersintheliteratureontheequitypremiumpuzzle
47:1831:128210:15:16:72:538:455:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and one that gave prominence to the role of heterogeneity.Mankiw(1986)showedthat,ina
47:1832:128294:16:16:72:535:439:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:two-period model with incomplete markets and idiosyncratic risk of the right form, one can
47:1833:128384:16:16:72:535:423:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:generate an equity premium as large as desired. However, researchers who followed up on
47:1834:128471:16:16:72:535:407:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this promising lead (Telmer(1993),Heaton and Lucas(1996), andKrusell and Smith(1997))
47:1835:128556:16:16:72:535:391:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:quickly came to a disappointing conclusion: once agents in these models are allowed to live
47:1836:128647:16:16:72:535:375:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:for multiple periods, trading a single risk-free asset yields sufficient consumption insurance,
47:1837:128742:16:20:72:314:359:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which in turn results in a tiny equity premium.
47:1838:128789:20:16:89:534:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This result—that a sufficiently long horizon can dramatically weaken the effects of in-
47:1839:128876:16:16:72:540:323:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:complete markets—is quite general.  In fact,Levine and Zame(2002)provedthatina
47:1840:128954:16:16:72:535:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:single good economy with no aggregate shocks if: (i) idiosyncratic income shocks follow a
47:1841:129043:16:16:72:535:291:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Markov process, (ii) marginal utility is convex, and (iii) all agents have access to a single
47:1842:129136:16:16:72:540:275:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:risk-free asset, then as individual’s subjective time discount factor (-)approachesunity,
47:1843:129225:16:16:72:535:259:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:then incomplete markets allocations (and utilities) converge to those from a complete mar-
47:1844:129315:16:15:72:535:243:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:kets economy with the same aggregate resources. Although Levine and Zame’s result is
47:1845:129399:15:16:72:535:228:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:theoretical for the limit of such economies (as-!1), it still sounds a cautionary note
47:1846:129485:16:16:72:535:212:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to researchers building incomplete markets models: unless shocks are extremely persistent
47:1847:129574:16:16:72:535:196:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and/or individuals are very impatient, these models are unlikely to generate results much
47:1848:129663:16:21:72:296:180:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:different from a representative-agent model.
47:1849:129707:21:15:89:535:159:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Constantinides and Duffie(1996) have shown one way to get around the problem of a long
47:1850:129793:15:16:72:535:144:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:horizon, which is also consistent with the message of Levine-Zame’s theorem. Essentially
47:1851:129881:16:16:72:535:128:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:they assume that individuals face permanent shocks, which eliminates the incentives to
47:1852:129967:16:16:72:535:112:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:smooth such shocks. Therefore, they behave as if they live in a static world and choose not
47:1853:130058:16:16:72:534:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to trade. Constantinides and Duffie also revive another feature ofMankiw(1986)’s model:
47:1854:130145:16:0:72:535:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic shocks must have larger variance in recessions (i.e., countercyclical variances)
48:1855:130241:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to generate a large equity premium. With these two features, they show that Mankiw’s
48:1856:130325:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:original insight can be made to work once again in an infinite horizon model.Storesletten
48:1857:130414:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:et al.(2007) found that a calibrated model along the lines suggested by Constantinides and
48:1858:130504:16:21:72:475:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Duffie can generate about 1/4 of the equity premium observed in the US data.
48:1859:130580:21:15:89:535:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The bottom line is that, loosely speaking, if incomplete markets matter in a model
48:1860:130662:15:16:72:535:612:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mainly through its effect on the consumption-saving decision, a long horizon can signifi-
48:1861:130751:16:16:72:535:596:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cantly weaken the bite that incomplete markets has. With a long enough horizon, agents
48:1862:130837:16:16:72:535:580:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:accumulate sufficient wealth and end up on the nearly linear portion of their savings func-
48:1863:130928:16:16:72:535:564:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tion, delivering results not far from a complete markets model. This is also the upshot of
48:1864:131018:16:34:72:257:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Krusell and Smith(1998)’s analysis.
48:1865:131053:34:28:72:420:514:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:7.2  Examples Where Heterogeneity Does Matter
48:1866:131098:28:16:72:535:486:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:There are many examples in which heterogeneity does matter for aggregate phenomena.
48:1867:131181:16:20:72:227:470:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Here, I review some examples.
48:1868:131210:20:16:89:535:450:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:First, aggregating heterogeneous-agent models can give rise to preferences for the repre-
48:1869:131299:16:16:72:535:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sentative agent that may have nothing to do with the preferences in the underlying model.
48:1870:131388:16:16:72:534:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:A well-known example of such a transformation was present in the early works ofHansen
48:1871:131473:16:16:72:535:402:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1985)andRogerson(1988), who showed that in a model in which individuals have no in-
48:1872:131557:16:16:72:535:386:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tensive margin of labor supply (i.e., zero Frisch labor supply elasticity), one can aggregate
48:1873:131650:16:15:72:535:370:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the model to find that the representative agent has linear preferences in leisure (i.e., infinite
48:1874:131747:15:16:72:535:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Frisch elasticity!).  This conclusion challenges one of the early justifications for building
48:1875:131840:16:16:72:535:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:models with micro-foundations, which was to bring evidence from micro data to bear on
48:1876:131925:16:16:72:535:323:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the calibration of macro models.  In an excellent survey paper,Browning et al.(1999)
48:1877:132009:16:16:72:535:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sounded an early cautionary note, giving several examples where this approach is fraught
48:1878:132097:16:20:72:136:291:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:with danger.
48:1879:132109:20:16:89:539:271:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Building on the earlier insights of Hansen and Rogerson,Chang and Kim(2006)con-
48:1880:132188:16:16:72:535:255:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:struct a model in which aggregate labor-supply elasticity depends on the reservation-wage
48:1881:132277:16:16:72:535:239:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:distribution in the population.  The economy is populated by households (husband and
48:1882:132361:16:16:72:535:223:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wife) who each supply labor only along the extensive margin: they either work full time or
48:1883:132451:16:16:72:535:207:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stay home. Workers are hit by idiosyncratic productivity shocks, causing them to move in
48:1884:132539:16:16:72:535:191:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and out of the labor market. The aggregate labor-supply elasticity of such an economy is
48:1885:132627:16:16:72:535:175:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:around 1, greater than a typical micro estimate and much greater than the Frisch elasticity
48:1886:132718:16:15:72:535:159:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:one would measure at the intensive margin (which is zero) in this model. The model thus
48:1887:132805:15:16:72:535:144:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:provides a reconciliation between the micro and macro labor-supply elasticities. In a sim-
48:1888:132895:16:16:72:539:128:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ilar vein,Chang et al.(2010)showthatpreferenceshiftersthatplayanimportantrolein
48:1889:132974:16:16:72:535:112:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discussions of aggregate policy are not invariant to policies if they are generated from the
48:1890:133066:16:16:72:535:96:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregation of a heterogeneous-agent model. Such a model also generates “wedges” at the
48:1891:133153:16:0:72:535:80:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:aggregate level that do not translate into any well-defined notion of preference shifters at
49:1892:133247:0:16:72:539:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the micro level.45Finally,Erosa et al.(2009)buildalifecyclemodeloflaborsupply,by
49:1893:133327:16:16:71:534:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:combining and extending the ideas introduced in earlier papers, such asChang and Kim
49:1894:133411:16:16:71:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2006)andRogerson and Wallenius(2009). Their goal is to build a model with empirically
49:1895:133497:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:plausible patterns of hours over the life cycle and examine the response elasticities of labor
49:1896:133591:16:21:71:262:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:supply to various policy experiments.
49:1897:133628:21:16:89:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In another context,Guvenen(2006) asks why macroeconomic models in the RBC tra-
49:1898:133706:16:15:71:534:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:dition typically need to assume a high elasticity of intertemporal substitution (EIS) to
49:1899:133794:15:16:71:534:580:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:explain output and investment fluctuations, whereas Euler equation regressions (such as
49:1900:133881:16:16:71:535:564:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in Hall(1988)andCampbell and Mankiw(1990)) that use aggregate consumption data
49:1901:133959:16:16:71:534:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:estimate a much smaller EIS (close to zero) to fit the data. He builds a model with two
49:1902:134046:16:16:71:535:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:types of agents who differ in their EIS. The model generates substantial wealth inequality
49:1903:134136:16:16:71:534:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and much smaller consumption inequality, both in line with the US data. Consequently,
49:1904:134221:16:16:71:534:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:capital and investment fluctuations are mainly driven by the rich (who hold almost all the
49:1905:134311:16:16:71:534:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wealth in the economy) and thus reflect the high EIS of this group. Consumption fluctua-
49:1906:134399:16:16:71:534:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tions, on the other hand, reflect an average that puts much more weight on the poor’s EIS,
49:1907:134489:16:15:71:534:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:who contribute significantly to aggregate consumption. Thus, a heterogeneous agent model
49:1908:134577:15:16:71:534:437:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is able to explain aggregate evidence that a single representative-agent model has trouble
49:1909:134667:16:21:71:105:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:fitting.
49:1910:134675:21:16:89:535:400:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:In an asset pricing context,Constantinides and Duffie(1996),Chan and Kogan(2002)
49:1911:134755:16:16:71:535:384:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and   Guvenen(2011)showasimilarresultforriskaversion.Constantinides and Duffie(1996)
49:1912:134839:16:16:71:534:368:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:show theoretically how the cross-sectional distribution of consumption in a heterogeneous-
49:1913:134929:16:16:71:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:agent model gets translated into a higher risk aversion for the representative agent.Guve-
49:1914:135019:16:15:71:534:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nen (2011) shows that in a calibrated model with limited stock market participation that
49:1915:135107:15:16:71:534:321:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:matches several asset pricing facts, the aggregate risk aversion is measured to be as high
49:1916:135197:16:16:71:534:305:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as 80, when the individuals’ risk aversion is only 2. These results as well as the papers
49:1917:135286:16:16:71:534:289:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:discussed above confirm and amplify the concerns originally highlighted byBrowning et al.
49:1918:135375:16:16:71:534:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(1999). The conclusion is that researchers must be very careful when using micro evidence
49:1919:135464:16:40:71:279:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to calibrate representative-agent models.
49:1920:135505:40:32:72:360:217:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:8ComputationandCalibration
49:1921:135531:32:16:72:535:185:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Because of their complexity, the overwhelming majority of models in this literature are
49:1922:135618:16:16:72:535:169:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:solved on a computer using numerical methods.46Thus, I now turn to a discussion of
49:1923:135700:16:16:72:535:153:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:computational issues that researchers often have to confront when solving models with
49:1924:135785:16:18:72:143:137:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneity.
49:1925:135799:18:12:81:379:119:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:45See Chari et al.(2007)forthedefinitionofbusinesscyclewedges.
49:1926:135861:12:15:81:534:107:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:46There are few examples of analytical solutions and theoretical results established with heterogeneous-
49:1927:135965:15:12:71:535:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:agent models. See, e.g.,Constantinides and Duffie(1996),Heathcote et al.(2007),Wang(2009),Guvenen
49:1928:136062:12:0:71:370:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:and Kuruscu(forthcoming), andRossi-Hansberg and Wright(2007).
50:1929:136125:0:29:72:441:696:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:8.1  Calibration and Estimation: Avoid Local Search
50:1930:136176:29:16:72:535:667:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Economists often need to minimize an objective function of multiple variables that has
50:1931:136262:16:16:72:535:651:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:lots of kinks, jaggedness, and deep ridges.  Consequently, the global minimum is often
50:1932:136348:16:16:72:535:635:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:surrounded by a large number of local minima. A typical example of such a problem arises
50:1933:136436:16:16:72:535:619:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:when a researcher tries to calibrate several structural parameters of an economic model
50:1934:136523:16:15:72:535:603:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by matching some data moments. Algorithms based on local optimization methods (e.g.,
50:1935:136607:15:16:72:535:588:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Newton-Raphson style derivative-based methods or Nelder-Mead simplex style routines)
50:1936:136691:16:16:72:535:572:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:very often get stuck in local minima, because the objective surface is typically very rough
50:1937:136782:16:21:72:145:556:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(non-smooth).
50:1938:136795:21:16:89:535:535:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:It is useful to understand some of the sources of this roughness. For example, linear in-
50:1939:136884:16:16:72:535:519:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:terpolation that is often used in approximating value functions or decision rules generates an
50:1940:136978:16:16:72:535:503:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:interpolated function that is non-differentiable (i.e., have kinks) at every knot point. Sim-
50:1941:137071:16:16:72:535:487:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ilarly, problems with (borrowing, portfolio, etc.) constraints can create significant kinks.
50:1942:137163:16:16:72:535:471:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Because researchers use a finite number of individuals to simulate data from the model
50:1943:137249:16:15:72:535:455:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(to compute moments) a small change in the parameter value (during the minimization
50:1944:137332:15:16:72:535:440:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the objective) can move some individuals across the threshold—from being constrained
50:1945:137419:16:16:72:535:424:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to unconstrained or vice versa—which can cause small jumps in the objective value. And
50:1946:137505:16:16:72:535:408:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sometimes, the moments that the researcher decides to match would be inherently discon-
50:1947:137592:16:16:72:535:392:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tinuous in the underlying parameters (with a finite number of individuals), such as the
50:1948:137679:16:16:72:535:376:143:g_d0_f6:143:g_d0_f2:medianof a distribution (e.g., wealth holdings).  Further compounding the problems, if
50:1949:137765:16:16:72:534:360:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the moments are not jointly sufficiently informative about the parameters to be calibrated,
50:1950:137856:16:16:72:535:344:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the objective function would be flat in certain directions. As can be expected, trying to
50:1951:137945:16:16:72:535:328:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:minimize a relatively flat function with lots of kinks, jaggedness, and even small jumps, can
50:1952:138038:16:20:72:235:312:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:be a very difficult task indeed.47
50:1953:138072:20:16:89:535:292:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:While the algorithm described here can be applied to the calibration of any model, it is
50:1954:138160:16:16:71:534:276:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:especially useful in models with heterogeneous agents—since such models are time consum-
50:1955:138248:16:16:71:534:260:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:ing to solve even once, an exhaustive search of the parameter space becomes prohibitively
50:1956:138337:16:41:71:329:244:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:costly (which could be feasible in simpler models).
50:1957:138388:41:29:72:532:203:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:8.2  A Simple Fully Parallelizable Global Optimization Algorithm
50:1958:138452:29:16:89:535:174:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Here, I describe a global optimization algorithm that I regularly use for calibrating
50:1959:138537:16:18:71:534:158:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:models and I have found it to be very practical and powerful. It is relatively straightforward
50:1960:138631:18:15:81:534:140:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:47One simple, but sometimes overlooked, point is that when minimizing an objective function of moments
50:1961:138733:15:12:71:534:125:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:to calibrate a model, one should use the same “seeds” for the random elements of the model that are used
50:1962:138837:12:12:71:534:113:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:to simulate the model in successive evaluations of the objective function. Otherwise, some of the change
50:1963:138941:12:12:71:534:101:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:in objective value will be due to the inherent randomness in different draws of random variables. This can
50:1964:139047:12:0:71:336:89:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:create significant problems with the minimization procedure.
51:1965:139109:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to implement, yet allows full parallelization across any number of CPU cores as well as across
51:1966:139203:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:any number of computers that are connected to the Internet. It requires no knowledge of
51:1967:139290:16:16:72:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:MPI, OpenMP, or related tools, and no knowledge of computer networking other than using
51:1968:139377:16:21:72:518:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:some commercially available synchronization tools (such as DropBox, SugarSync, etc.).
51:1969:139462:21:16:89:535:627:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:A broad outline of the algorithm is as follows. As with many global algorithms, this
51:1970:139546:16:16:72:535:611:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:procedure combines a global stage with a local search stage that is restarted at various
51:1971:139634:16:16:72:535:595:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:locations in the parameter space. First, we would like to search the parameter space as
51:1972:139721:16:16:72:535:579:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:thoroughly as possible, but do so in as efficient a way as possible. Thoroughness is essential
51:1973:139815:16:15:72:535:563:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:because we want to be sure that we found the true global minimum, so we are willing to
51:1974:139901:15:16:72:535:548:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sacrifice some speed to ensure this. The algorithm proceeds by taking an initial starting
51:1975:139990:16:16:72:536:532:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:point (chosen in a manner described momentarily) and conducting a local search from that
51:1976:140078:16:16:72:536:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:point on until the minimization routine converges as specified by some tolerance. For local
51:1977:140169:16:16:72:535:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:search, I typically rely on the Nelder-Mead’s downhill simplex algorithm because it does
51:1978:140257:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:not require derivative information (that may be inaccurate given the approximation errors
51:1979:140346:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in the model’s solution algorithm).48The minimum function value as well as the parameter
51:1980:140434:16:16:71:534:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:combination that attained that minimum are recorded in a file saved on the computer’s hard
51:1981:140524:16:16:71:534:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:disk. The algorithm then picks the next “random” starting point and repeats the previous
51:1982:140612:16:15:71:534:420:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:step of local minimization. The results are then added to the previous file, which records
51:1983:140702:15:21:71:297:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:all the local minima found up to that point.
51:1984:140746:21:16:89:535:384:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Of course, the most obvious algorithm would be to keep doing a very large number of
51:1985:140829:16:16:71:534:368:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:restarts of this sort and take the minimum of all the minima found in the process. But
51:1986:140915:16:16:71:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this would be very time consuming and would not be particularly efficient. Moreover, in
51:1987:141002:16:16:71:534:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:many cases, the neighborhood of the global minimum can feature many deep ridges and
51:1988:141085:16:16:71:534:320:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:kinks nearby, which requires more extensive searching near the global minimum, whereas
51:1989:141171:16:16:71:534:304:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the proposed approach would devote as much time to points far away from the true global
51:1990:141258:16:16:71:534:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:minimum as to the points near it. Further, if the starting points are chosen literally ran-
51:1991:141349:16:15:71:534:272:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:domly, this would also create potentially large efficiency losses, because these points have a
51:1992:141443:15:16:71:534:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:non-negligible chance of falling near points previously tried. Because those areas have been
51:1993:141535:16:21:71:356:241:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:previously searched, devoting more time is not optimal.
51:1994:141590:21:16:89:540:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Abetterapproachistouse“quasi-random”numberstogeneratethestartingpoints.
51:1995:141661:16:16:71:534:204:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Quasi-random numbers (also called Low-discrepancy sequences) are sequences of determin-
51:1996:141748:16:16:71:534:188:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:istic numbers that spread to any space in the maximally separated way. They avoid the
51:1997:141833:16:16:71:534:172:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:pitfall of random draws that may end up being too close to each other. Each draw in the
51:1998:141920:16:16:71:534:156:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sequence “knows” the location of previous points drawn and attempts to fill the gaps as
51:1999:142007:16:17:71:535:140:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:evenly as possible.49Among a variety of sequences proposed in the literature, the Sobol’
51:2000:142095:17:16:81:534:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:48An alternative that can be much faster but requires a bit more tweaking for best performance is the
51:2001:142196:16:8:71:486:107:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:trust region method ofZhang et al.(2010)thatbuildsonPowell(2009)’s BOBYQA algorithm.
51:2002:142280:8:16:81:534:99:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:49Another common application of low-discrepancy sequences is in quasi-Monte Carlo integration, where
51:2003:142380:16:0:71:431:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:they have been found to improve time-to-accuracy by several orders of magnitude.
52:2004:142462:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:sequence is generally viewed to be superior in most practical applications, having a very
52:2005:142551:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:uniform filling of the space (i.e., maximally separated) even for a small number of points
52:2006:142641:16:20:72:423:664:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:drawn as well as a very fast algorithm that generates the sequence.50
52:2007:142710:20:16:89:535:644:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Next, how do we use the accumulated information from previous restarts? As suggested
52:2008:142794:16:16:71:534:628:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by genetic algorithm heuristics, I combine information from previous best runs to adaptively
52:2009:142886:16:16:71:534:612:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:direct the new restarts to areas that appear more promising. This is explained further below.
52:2010:142979:16:20:71:267:596:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Now for the specifics of the algorithm.
52:2011:143018:20:21:89:497:576:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f13:Letpbe aJ-dimensional parameter vector with generic elementpj,j=1,..,J.
52:2012:143089:21:27:89:219:555:143:g_d0_f52:143:g_d0_f2:•Step 0.Initialization:
52:2013:143112:27:16:112:535:528:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:1. Determine bounds for each parameter, outside of which the objective function
52:2014:143191:16:21:127:278:512:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:should be set to a high value.
52:2015:143221:21:15:112:535:491:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:2. Generate a sequence of Sobol’ numbers with a sequence length ofImax(the maxi-
52:2016:143301:15:16:127:535:476:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:mum anticipated number of restarts in the global stage). Set the global iteration
52:2017:143382:16:28:127:198:460:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:numberi=1.
52:2018:143392:28:28:89:218:432:143:g_d0_f52:143:g_d0_f2:•Step 1.Global stage:
52:2019:143413:28:20:112:403:404:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:1. Draw theith(vector) value in the Sobol’ sequence:si.
52:2020:143468:20:16:112:539:384:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:2. Ifi>1,openandreadfromthetextfile“saved_parameters.dat”thefunction
52:2021:143536:16:16:127:535:368:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:values (and corresponding parameter vectors) of previously found local minima.
52:2022:143614:16:16:127:535:352:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Denote the lowest function value found as of iterationi-1asflowi-1and the
52:2023:143687:16:20:127:332:336:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:corresponding parameter vector asplowi-1.
52:2024:143728:20:28:112:409:316:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:3. Generate a starting point for the local stage as follows:
52:2025:143788:28:15:114:535:288:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–Ifi<Imin(<Imax)then usesias the initial guess:Si=si.Here,Iminis the
52:2026:143856:15:16:127:535:273:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:threshold below which we use fully quasi-random starting points in the global
52:2027:143933:16:21:127:156:257:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stage.
52:2028:143939:21:16:114:535:236:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–Ifi-Imin,take the initial guess to be a convex combination ofsiand the
52:2029:144010:16:15:127:535:220:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f14:parameter value that generated the best local minima so far:Si=(1-✓i)si+
52:2030:144082:15:16:127:541:205:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f2:✓plowi-1. The parameter✓i2[0,✓]with✓<1, and increases withi.Forexample,
52:2031:144153:16:16:127:534:189:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Ifoundthataconvexincreasingfunction,suchas✓i=min[✓,(i/Imax)2], works
52:2032:144221:16:20:127:457:173:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:well in some applications. An alternative heuristic is given later.
52:2033:144288:20:16:114:534:153:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–As✓iis increased local searches are restarted from a narrower part of the param-
52:2034:144369:16:18:127:407:137:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:eter space that yielded the lowest local minima before.
52:2035:144424:18:15:81:534:119:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:50In a wide range of optimization problems,Liberti and Kucherenko(2005)andKucherenko and Sytsko
52:2036:144519:15:12:71:538:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:(2005)findthatSobol’sequencesoutperformsHoltonsequences,bothintermsofcomputationtimeand
52:2037:144606:12:12:71:534:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:probability of finding the global optimum. The Holton sequence is particularly weak in high dimensional
52:2038:144709:12:0:71:126:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:applications.
53:2039:144724:0:29:89:211:696:143:g_d0_f52:143:g_d0_f2:•Step 2:Local stage:
53:2040:144744:29:16:114:534:667:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–UsingSias a starting point, use the downhill simplex algorithm to search for a
53:2041:144823:16:16:127:535:651:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:local minimum. (For the other vertices of the simplex, randomly draw starting
53:2042:144900:16:21:127:384:635:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:points within the bounds of the parameter space).
53:2043:144949:21:16:114:535:614:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–Stop when either (i) a certain tolerance has been achieved, (ii) function values do
53:2044:145033:16:16:127:535:598:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:not improve more than a certain amount, or (iii) the maximum iteration number
53:2045:145110:16:21:127:181:582:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is reached.
53:2046:145121:21:15:114:535:561:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–Opensaved_parameters.datand record the local minimum found (function
53:2047:145190:15:29:127:244:546:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:value and parameters).
53:2048:145212:29:29:89:229:517:143:g_d0_f52:143:g_d0_f2:•Step 3.Stopping Rule:
53:2049:145234:29:38:114:535:488:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:–Stop if the termination criterion described below is satisfied. If not go to step 1.
53:2050:145319:38:16:71:534:450:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Termination Criterion.One useful heuristic criterion relies on a Bayesian procedure
53:2051:145402:16:16:71:534:434:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that estimates the probability that the next local search will find a new local minimum
53:2052:145489:16:15:71:534:418:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:based on the rate at which new local minima have been located in past searches. More
53:2053:145573:15:16:71:534:403:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:concretely, ifWdifferent local minima have been found afterKlocal searches started from
53:2054:145660:16:29:71:538:387:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:asetofuniformlydistributedpoints,thentheexpectationofthenumberoflocalminimais
53:2055:145737:29:29:228:378:358:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f14:Wexp=W(K−1)/(K−W−2)
53:2056:145756:29:16:71:535:329:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:provided thatK>W+2. The searching procedure is terminated ifWexp<W+0.5. The
53:2057:145831:16:16:72:535:313:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:idea is that, after a while of searching, if subsequent restarts keep finding one of the the
53:2058:145923:16:16:72:535:297:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:same local minima found before, the chances of improvement in subsequent searches is not
53:2059:146011:16:16:72:535:281:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:worth the additional time cost. Although this is generally viewed as one of the most reliable
53:2060:146104:16:21:72:348:265:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heuristics, care must be applied as with any heuristic.
53:2061:146159:21:16:89:535:244:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Notice also thatWexpcan be used to adaptively increase the value of✓iin the global
53:2062:146241:16:16:72:535:228:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:stage (Step 1(3) above).  The idea is that as subsequent global re-starts do not yield a
53:2063:146329:16:15:72:535:212:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:new local minimum with a high enough probability, it is time to narrow down the search
53:2064:146415:15:16:72:535:197:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and further explore areas of promising local minima. Because jaggedness and deep ridges
53:2065:146502:16:16:72:535:181:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cause local search methods to often get stuck, we want to explore promising areas more
53:2066:146588:16:21:72:130:165:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:thoroughly.
53:2067:146599:21:16:89:535:144:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:One can improve upon this basic algorithm in various ways. I am going to mention a
53:2068:146681:16:0:72:231:128:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:few that seem worth exploring.
54:2069:146713:0:16:72:535:696:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Refinements: Clustering and Pre-testing.First, suppose that in iterationk,the
54:2070:146790:16:16:72:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:proposed starting pointSkends up being “close” to one of the previous minima, sayplown,
54:2071:146877:16:16:71:535:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f13:forn<k. Then it is likely that the search starting fromSkwill end up converging toplown.
54:2072:146965:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:But then we have wasted an entire cycle of local search without gaining anything. To prevent
54:2073:147057:16:16:71:533:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:this, one heuristic (called “clustering methods”) proceeds by defining a “region of attraction”
54:2074:147152:16:16:71:535:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(which is essentially aJ-dimensional ball centered) around each one of the local minima
54:2075:147239:16:16:71:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:found so far.51Then the algorithm would discard a proposed re-starting point if it falls into
54:2076:147332:16:16:71:534:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the region attraction of any previous local minima. Because the local minimization stage is
54:2077:147423:16:15:71:534:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the most computationally intensive step, this refinement of restarting the local search only
54:2078:147515:15:16:71:534:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:once in a given region of attraction can result in significant computational gains. Extensive
54:2079:147608:16:21:71:501:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:surveys of clustering methods can be found inRinnooy Kan and Timmer(1987a,b).
54:2080:147685:21:16:89:535:516:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Second, one can add a “pre-test” stage whereNpoints from the Sobol’ sequence are
54:2081:147765:16:16:71:539:500:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f13:evaluated before any local search (i.e., in Step 0 above), and only a subset ofN⇤<N
54:2082:147848:16:16:72:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:points with lowest objective values are used as seeds in the local search. The remaining
54:2083:147936:16:16:72:536:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:points as well as regions of attraction around it are ignored as not promising. Notice that
54:2084:148027:16:37:72:447:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:while this stage can improve speed, it trades offreliability in the process.
54:2085:148103:37:16:72:534:415:143:g_d0_f20:143:g_d0_f2:Narrowing Down the Search Area.The filesaved_parameters.datcontains a lot of
54:2086:148179:16:16:72:535:399:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:useful information gathered in each iteration to the global stage, which can be used more
54:2087:148268:16:16:72:534:383:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:efficiently as follows. As noted, the Nelder-Mead algorithm requiresJ+1candidate points
54:2088:148355:16:16:72:535:367:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as inputs (the vertices of theJ-dimensional simplex). One of these points is given bySi,
54:2089:148443:16:16:71:534:351:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:chosen as described above; the other vertices were drawn randomly. But as we accumulate
54:2090:148530:16:16:71:534:335:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:more information with every iteration on the global stage, if we keep finding local minima
54:2091:148620:16:16:71:534:319:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that seem to concentrate in certain regions, it makes sense to narrow the range of values
54:2092:148709:16:15:71:534:303:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:from which we pick the vertices. One way to do this is as follows: After a sufficiently large
54:2093:148802:15:16:71:534:288:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:number of re-starts have been completed, rank all the function values and take the lowest
54:2094:148891:16:16:71:535:272:143:g_d0_f54:143:g_d0_f2:x% of values (e.g., 10% or 20%). Then for each dimension, pick the minimum (callpjmin)and
54:2095:148980:16:16:71:535:256:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:maximum parameter value (callpjmax)within this set of minima. Then to generate vertices,
54:2096:149068:16:16:72:535:240:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:take randomly sampled points betweenpjminandpjmaxin each dimensionj. This allows the
54:2097:149152:16:16:71:534:224:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:simplex algorithm to search more intensively in a narrower area, which can improve results
54:2098:149242:16:16:71:534:208:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:very quickly when there are ridges or jaggedness in the objective function that makes the
54:2099:149331:16:18:71:188:192:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:algorithm to get stuck.
54:2100:149354:18:15:81:535:174:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:51While different formulas have been proposed for determining the optimal radius, these formulas contain
54:2101:149458:15:0:72:466:159:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:some undetermined coefficients which makes them less than useful in real life applications.
55:2102:149551:0:29:72:297:696:206:g_d0_f11:206:g_d0_f11:8.3  Parallelizing the Algorithm
55:2103:149583:29:16:72:535:667:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The algorithm can be parallelized in a relatively straightforward manner.52The basic idea
55:2104:149672:16:16:72:535:651:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:is to let each CPU core perform a separate local search in a different part of the parameter
55:2105:149764:16:16:72:535:635:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:space, which is a time-consuming process. If we can do many such searches simultaneously,
55:2106:149853:16:16:72:535:619:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:we can speed up the solution dramatically. One factor that makes parallelization simple is
55:2107:149943:16:15:72:535:603:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that fact that the CPU cores do not need to communicate with each other during the local
55:2108:150031:15:16:72:535:588:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:search stage. In-between the local stages, each CPU core will contribute its findings (the
55:2109:150121:16:16:72:535:572:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:last local minimum it found along with the corresponding parameter vector) to the collective
55:2110:150213:16:16:72:535:556:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:wisdom recorded insaved_parameters.datand also get the latest updated information
55:2111:150294:16:16:72:535:540:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:about the best local minimum found so far from the same file. Thus, as long as all CPU cores
55:2112:150386:16:16:72:538:524:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:have access to the same copy of the filesaved_parameters.dat,parallelizationrequiresno
55:2113:150472:16:21:72:498:508:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:more than a few lines for housekeeping across CPUs. Here are some more specifics.
55:2114:150553:21:16:89:535:487:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Suppose that we have a workstation withNCPU cores (for example,N=4, 6, or 12).
55:2115:150631:16:16:71:534:471:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The first modification we need to make is to change the program to distinguish between
55:2116:150717:16:15:71:535:455:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the different “copies” of the code, running on different CPU cores. This can be done by
55:2117:150804:15:16:71:534:440:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:simply having the program ask the user (only once, upon starting the code) to input an
55:2118:150890:16:16:71:535:424:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:integer value,n,between1andN, which uniquely identifies the “sequence number” of the
55:2119:150974:16:16:71:535:408:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:particular instance of the program running. Then openNterminal windows and launch a
55:2120:151057:16:16:71:534:392:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:copy of the program in each window. Then for each one, enter a unique sequence number
55:2121:151142:16:21:71:140:376:143:g_d0_f13:143:g_d0_f2:n=1,2..., N.
55:2122:151154:21:16:89:535:355:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Upon starting, each program will first simulate the same quasi-random sequence re-
55:2123:151236:16:16:71:535:339:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:gardless ofn, but each run will pick a different element of this sequence as its own seed.
55:2124:151326:16:16:71:534:323:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:For simplicity, suppose runnchooses thenthelement of the sequence as its seed and
55:2125:151407:16:15:71:534:307:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:launches a local search from that point. After completion, each run will open the same
55:2126:151493:15:16:71:534:292:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:filesaved_parameters.datand record the local minimum and parameter value it finds.53
55:2127:151577:16:16:72:535:276:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Now suppose that all copies of the program complete their respective first local searches, so
55:2128:151670:16:16:72:535:260:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:there areNlines, each written by a different CPU core, in the filesaved_parameters.dat.
55:2129:151757:16:16:71:534:244:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Then each run will start its second iteration and pick as its next seed the(N+n)thelement
55:2130:151846:16:16:71:534:228:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of the quasi-random sequence. When the total number of iterations across all CPUs exceed
55:2131:151934:16:16:71:535:212:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:some thresholdImin, then we would like to combine the quasi-random draw with the pre-
55:2132:152019:16:16:72:535:196:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:vious best local minima as described in Step 1.3 above. This is simple since all runs have
55:2133:152109:16:18:72:346:180:143:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f4:access to the same copy ofsaved_parameters.dat.54
55:2134:152158:18:15:81:534:162:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:52I am assuming here that a compiled language, such as Fortran or C, is used to write the program. So
55:2135:152259:15:9:71:433:147:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:multiple parallel copies of the same code can be run in different terminal windows.
55:2136:152342:9:15:81:534:138:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:53Because this opening and writing stage takes a fraction of a second, the likelihood that two or more
55:2137:152444:15:9:71:421:123:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:programs access the file simultaneously and create a run-time error is negligible.
55:2138:152526:9:15:81:535:114:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:54It is often useful for each run to keep track of thetotalnumber of local searches completed by all
55:2139:152626:15:12:71:535:99:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:CPUs—call thisNLast.Forexample,sometimestheincreasein✓ican be linked toNLast. This number
55:2140:152715:12:0:71:539:87:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:can be read offas the total number of lines recorded up to that point insaved_parameters.dat.Another
56:2141:152817:0:16:89:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Notice that this parallelization method is completely agnostic about whether the CPU
56:2142:152901:16:16:71:535:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:cores are on the same PC or distributed across many PCsas long asall computers keep
56:2143:152984:16:16:71:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:synchronized copies ofsaved_parameters.dat. This can be achieved by using a synchro-
56:2144:153068:16:16:71:534:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:nization service like DropBox. This feature easily allows one to harness the computational
56:2145:153158:16:47:71:520:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:power of many idle PCs distributed geographically with varying speeds and CPU cores.
56:2146:153242:47:33:72:438:585:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:9FutureDirectionsandFurtherReading
56:2147:153276:33:16:72:535:552:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:This article has surveyed the current state of the heterogeneous-agent models literature and
56:2148:153368:16:16:72:535:536:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:drew several conclusions. First, two key ingredients in such models are (i) the magnitudes
56:2149:153458:16:15:72:535:520:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:and types of risk that the model-builder feeds into the model and (ii) the insurance oppor-
56:2150:153549:15:16:72:534:505:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:tunities allowed in the economy. In many cases, it is difficult, if not impossible, to measure
56:2151:153643:16:16:72:535:489:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:each component separately. In other words, the assumptions a researcher makes regarding
56:2152:153730:16:16:72:535:473:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:insurance opportunities will typically affect the inference drawn about the magnitudes of
56:2153:153819:16:16:72:535:457:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:risks and vice versa. Further complicating the problem is the measurement of risk: individ-
56:2154:153910:16:16:72:535:441:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:uals often have more information than the econometrician about future changes in their life.
56:2155:154002:16:16:72:535:425:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:So, for example, a rise or fall in income that the econometrician may view as a “shock” may
56:2156:154093:16:16:72:535:409:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:in fact be partially or completely anticipated by the individual. This suggests that equating
56:2157:154186:16:16:72:535:393:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:income movements observed in the data with risk (as is often done in the literature) is likely
56:2158:154280:16:15:72:535:377:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:to overstate the true magnitude. This entanglement of “risk,” “anticipated changes,” and
56:2159:154368:15:16:72:534:362:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:“insurance” presents a difficult challenge to researchers in this area. Although some recent
56:2160:154460:16:21:72:301:346:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:progress has been made, more work remains.
56:2161:154502:21:16:89:540:325:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Anumberofsurveyscontainveryvaluablematerialthatarecomplementarytothis
56:2162:154571:16:16:72:541:309:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:paper.  First,Heathcote et al.(2009)isanotherrecentsurveyofquantitativemacroe-
56:2163:154649:16:16:72:535:293:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:conomics with heterogeneous households that is complementary to this paper.  Second,
56:2164:154733:16:16:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Browning et al.(1999)containsanextensivereviewofmicromodelsthatareoftenused
56:2165:154808:16:16:72:535:261:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:as the foundations of heterogeneous-agent models. It highlights several pitfalls in trying to
56:2166:154901:16:16:72:538:245:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:calibrate macro models using micro evidence. Third,Meghir and Pistaferri(2011)provides
56:2167:154987:16:15:72:535:229:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:a comprehensive treatment of how earnings dynamics affect life cycle consumption choice,
56:2168:155075:15:16:72:535:214:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:which is closely related to the issues discussed in Section 4 of this survey. Finally, because
56:2169:155169:16:16:72:535:198:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:heterogeneous-agent models use micro survey data in increasingly sophisticated ways, a
56:2170:155255:16:16:72:535:182:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:solid understanding of issues related to measurement error (which is pervasive in micro
56:2171:155342:16:16:72:535:166:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:data) is essential. Failure to understand such problems can wreak havoc with the empirical
56:2172:155432:16:22:72:510:150:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:analysis.Bound et al.(2001)isanextensiveandauthoritativesurveyofthesubject.
56:2173:155507:22:12:72:535:128:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:use of this index is for determining which point in the sequence to select as the next seed point. So as
56:2174:155611:12:12:72:535:116:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:opposed to runnselecting the(kN+n)thpoint in the sequence wherekis the number of local searches
56:2175:155706:12:12:71:535:104:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:completed by runn,itcouldjustpickthe(NLast+ 1)thnumber in the sequence. This avoids leaving gaps
56:2176:155802:12:12:72:535:92:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:in the sequence for seeds, in case some CPUs are much faster than others and hence finish many more local
56:2177:155907:12:0:72:163:80:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:searches than others.
57:2178:155930:0:16:89:535:696:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:The introduction of families into incomplete markets models represents an exciting area
57:2179:156017:16:16:71:534:680:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:of current research. For many questions of empirical relevance, the interactions taking place
57:2180:156110:16:16:71:534:664:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:within a household (implicit insurance, bargaining, etc.) can have first-order effects on how
57:2181:156203:16:16:71:535:648:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:individuals respond to idiosyncratic changes. To give a few examples,Gallipoli and Turner
57:2182:156292:16:16:71:538:632:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:(2011)documentthatthelaborsupplyresponsestodisabilityshocksofsingleworkersare
57:2183:156369:16:16:71:534:616:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:larger and more persistent than those of married workers. They argue that an important
57:2184:156455:16:16:71:535:600:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:part of this difference has to do with the fact that couples are able to optimally change
57:2185:156544:16:16:71:534:584:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:their time (and task) allocation within household in response to disability, an option not
57:2186:156634:16:15:71:534:568:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:available to singles. This finding suggests that modeling households would be important for
57:2187:156725:15:16:71:537:553:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:understanding the design of disability insurance policies. Similarly,Guner et al.(2010)show
57:2188:156816:16:16:72:535:537:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:that to quantify the effects of alternative tax reforms, it is important to take into account
57:2189:156909:16:16:72:535:521:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:the joint nature of household labor supply. In fact, it is hard to imagine any distributional
57:2190:157002:16:21:72:463:505:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:issue for which the household structure does not figure in an important way.
57:2191:157078:21:16:89:535:484:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Another promising area is the richer modeling of household finances in an era of ever-
57:2192:157164:16:16:72:535:468:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:increasing sophistication in financial services. The Great Recession, which was accompanied
57:2193:157255:16:16:72:535:452:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:by a housing market crash and soaring personal bankruptcies, home foreclosures, and so
57:2194:157341:16:15:72:535:436:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:on, has created a renewed sense of urgency for understanding household balance sheets.
57:2195:157427:15:16:72:535:421:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:Developments on two fronts—advances in theoretical modeling as discussed in Section 4
57:2196:157512:16:16:72:535:405:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:combined with richer data sources on credit histories and mortgages that are increasingly
57:2197:157601:16:47:72:487:389:143:g_d0_f2:143:g_d0_f2:becoming available to researchers—will make faster progress feasible in this area.
